I answered enthusiastically to Maristel’s suggestion. While Isezaki-san seemed confident in potion-making, she hadn’t mentioned having any equipment ready. So it would be better to use Maristel’s setup.

“But, Husband…”

Isezaki-san seemed hesitant, furrowing her brows slightly. But I decided to push forward.

“Come on, Isezaki-san. It’s a kind offer, and it would be quicker this way, don’t you think?”

“Just let her accept my thanks, Isezaki. What’s the harm?”

Isezaki-san looked at the two of us in turn, her expression troubled. Eventually, she sighed softly, as if resigning herself to the situation.

“Yes… I suppose so. We’ll take you up on that offer, then…”

She forced a slightly awkward smile.

+++

# 208. Maristel's Atelier

Slurping down our cup noodles, Isezaki and I finished our meal feeling slightly unsatisfied. Maristel, eager to get going, led us into the adjacent room. 

The room appeared to be Maristel’s bedroom. It was simple, with a large double bed that seemed too spacious for just one person and a small round table with what looked like a bottle of wine on it. However, in one corner of the room, there was an iron door. When opened, a set of stairs descended slowly downward. Apparently, Maristel’s workshop was down there.

“Wow, this is more serious than I expected…” 

“Right? This whole area used to be a mining site. This staircase is from a test dig a long time ago. Thanks to this tunnel, I had them build my house here. As a necromancer, you need a room where light doesn’t reach, after all.”

I see, she had mentioned earlier that spirit bodies are weak to light. For a necromancer, a dark room like this must be essential.

We stepped through the iron door and descended into the cool air of the underground. Eventually, we arrived at a spacious cavity. The ceiling was reasonably high, and the room was about the size of a small convenience store. The faint light from glow moss clinging to the walls made it possible to see the room’s shape, though the details inside were still unclear.

“So, what do you think? This is my workshop,” 

Maristel said proudly, pressing a switch on the wall. Suddenly, magic lamps lit up, revealing the interior of the room.

“Whoa…”

I couldn’t help but let out a gasp. Up until now, Maristel had always seemed to own very few belongings, but this underground room more than made up for it. It was packed with all sorts of items.

On the shelves were glass bottles filled with colorful liquids and strange, unknown tools. On the desk were piles of scrolls and thick tomes stacked haphazardly. Animal skulls with horns hung on the walls, along with tapestries depicting strange magical circles. In the back of the room sat a large cauldron big enough to fit a person inside.

This was exactly what you’d expect from a witch’s workshop. Honestly, it stirred a bit of the childish excitement I had in my younger, more imaginative days.

“I had that bearded guy and his team bring all this stuff over from the secret base in the magic stone mine.”

Apparently, she had originally been using the large cavity at the back of the magic stone mine, where Isezaki had been held captive, as both her workshop and living space. Moving all these things must have been quite a task for Captain Hige and his men.

Incidentally, when they first moved the items into the mine, they used the same [Portal Port] that was also used in Isezaki’s kidnapping.

“Now then, you two picked a lot of Healer’s herbs, didn’t you? I’ve made potions with those before, and I’m quite confident in my skills. Come on, Matsunaga, give me the herbs. I’ll show you a special demonstration of potion crafting,” 

She said, drawing out the moment for effect. Maristel pulled out a tool from the shelf that looked like an ab roller but was apparently an ancient herbal grinder called a “yagen.” She planned to crush the herbs with it.

(Note:

            Ab Roller                              Yagen

)

“Alright, Maristel, I’ll leave it to you,” 

I said, pulling out a bundle of Healer’s herbs from my [Storage Space] and handing it to her. But then—

“Um, but Husband…” 

Isezaki tugged at my sleeve nervously, her face tense.

“Oh my, what’s wrong, Isezaki? No need to hold back,” 

Maristel said, snatching the Healer’s herbs from my hand with a swift motion.

“Ah…” 

Isezaki let out a soft sound, but Maristel paid no attention to her. With practiced hands, she spread the herbs across the yagen and began grinding them—**_*gori gori gori gori*_**—with a steady rhythm.

“Heh heh… To amateurs like you, this might look like a simple task, but it’s not. You can’t just crush them with brute force, you know? You have to press harder on the tough fibers and go gently on the soft parts. The key is to make the fiber texture as uniform as possible. If you don’t do it properly, the mixture will be inconsistent, and you won’t get the potion you were expecting. The basics of potion-making are crucial—very crucial. Those who neglect the basics will never earn the favor of the god of medicine.”

It seemed Maristel took her potion-making seriously.

She boasted endlessly, spouting trivia as she ground the herbs with great care and strength, making a persistent **_*gori gori*_** sound. 

After some time of this grinding…

Perhaps it was due to the considerable effort and focus she was putting in, but beads of sweat were forming on Maristel’s forehead. As she wiped her brow with her arm to keep the sweat from dripping, she muttered:

“_Huff, huff_… almost done, just a little longer. _Huff, huff_… Once I use some high-quality holy water after this, I should be able to make an extraordinary potion… Well, I guess I have no choice. For your sake, I’ll use my special holy water this time—”

“Uh, um, Maristel!” 

Just then, Isezaki, who had been acting strange for a while now, interrupted with a stiff voice.

“Come on, Isezaki, I told you, you don’t have to hold back. You helped me name the fortress, after all, so I owe you one. And this is just me paying you back—”

“N-no, really, it’s fine. I understand your feelings… but, well…”

“Huh? What do you mean?”

Maristel stopped her work for a moment, looking confused as she stared at Isezaki, who was fumbling to find the right words. 

But Isezaki, still with a tense expression, turned her face toward me. 

“A-anyway! Um, Husband. Could you please take out the Healer’s herb and the thermos with the tea from earlier?”

“Huh? Uh, sure…”

I had no idea what was going on, but seeing Isezaki’s serious expression, I did as she asked and pulled the Healer’s herb and the thermos from the [Storage Space].

“Thank you. As for the tea… I’m sorry, but I’ll be throwing it out.”

Isezaki tipped the thermos upside down, pouring the tea down the drain. Then, she firmly packed the Healer’s herb into the now-empty thermos.

“W-what!?”

“What are you doing, Isezaki!? That’s such a waste!” 

Both Maristel and I shouted in surprise. But Isezaki, unfazed, held the thermos toward me.

“Husband, for now, please just watch without saying anything. Next, could you fill this thermos with water?”

“O-okay. Water, huh… Umm, is tap water fine?”

“Yes, that will be just fine.”

Following her instructions, I poured some of the stored tap water from my [Storage Space] into the thermos, letting it flow until it was filled to the brim.

“…Alright, that’s enough. Thank you so much. Now, if you would…”

After closing the thermos lid, Isezaki glanced up at me with a soft, pleading look. I knew what this meant—she was asking for a mana supply. At least that much was clear.

I gently took her hand. As she closed her eyes, she raised the thermos over her head with her other hand and chanted:

“[Potion Creation]—”

—In that instant, a blinding light radiated from Isezaki, spreading outward and enveloping the entire lab in a mystical white glow.

+++

# 209. High-Quality Tap Water

After a moment, the light dimmed, and I slowly opened my eyes. I had narrowed them due to the brightness. 

Standing before me, Isezaki-san clutched a thermos against her chest. She was hesitating before she spoke timidly.  

“Um… well, it’s finished…”  

“Huh…?”  

“What do you mean, it’s finished?” 

Without a word, Isezaki-san opened the lid of the thermos and began carefully pouring the contents into the lid cup. What poured out wasn’t the usual tap water.  

To be precise, it wasn’t tap water *anymore*.  

The liquid wasn’t clear but had a faint bluish tint. Depending on the angle, it shimmered as if reflecting light.  

“P-please, have some…”  

Isezaki-san nervously offered the cup filled with the mysterious liquid to Maristel, who tilted her head quizzically but accepted it without hesitation. Upon seeing the contents, however, Maristel furrowed her brows.  

“Th-this is…!?”  

Eyes wide, Maristel inspected the liquid from various angles. She sniffed it cautiously before bursting into a flustered reaction.  

“Wait, no, hold on. Hold on, Isezaki… could this be…?”  

Isezaki-san nodded silently. Maristel began trembling, her shoulders quaking uncontrollably.  

“No way… no freaking way… Why on earth did you manage to create a potion!?” 

“Huh? A potion? Are you saying the water from this thermos is a potion?”  

“Yes! And it looks *extremely* high quality, too… But, no, there’s no way, right? Surely not…?”  

Maristel’s face twisted with skepticism, but Isezaki-san quietly muttered, 

“Just try drinking it…”  

“You’re right. Okay, I will…”  

After staring intently at the cup, Maristel made up her mind and tilted the cup. She gulped down the liquid.  

“Pwah! It doesn’t taste like anything, but—”  

Maristel grimaced, wiping her mouth with the back of her hand. Her tense expression soon melted away completely.  

“Ahhh~! This is incredible, absolutely incredible~! Aah, ah, ah~! Nooo, my knees are giving out~!”  

Letting out oddly suggestive moans, Maristel collapsed to the ground. She sat dazedly with a blissful look on her face, as if she were floating on a cloud.  

“………..Is this potion really that amazing?”  

“Yes, it’s amazing… Matsunaga, why don’t you try it? I might’ve gone a bit… overboard~♡” Maristel, with a dreamy smile, held out the partially used cup to me.  

If it’s that incredible, I couldn’t resist the urge to try it. Swallowing hard, I reached out for the cup she offered.  

“Alright then, let me—”  

“No! Husband, you should have this instead!”  

Before I could take the cup, Isezaki-san intervened. She shoved the thermos directly to my mouth without warning.  

“_Gulp, gulp, gulp, gulp!_”  

The potion was poured straight down my throat in an unceremonious manner.  

“Pwah! What the heck, Isezaki-san!? Why’d you do that all of a sudden?”  

“S-sorry! I just… couldn’t help myself…”  

Maybe she wanted me to try a fresh batch instead of the leftovers. Still, shoving it down my throat directly seemed excessive. Thankfully, I didn’t choke on it. Just as I was thinking that—  

Something began to change in my body.  

“Huh? Ohhh…?”  

After a day of climbing mountains and fighting battles, I had pushed myself to the limit. While I had been careful not to show any signs of exhaustion around Isezaki-san, my body was undeniably at its breaking point.  

But in that moment, all my fatigue vanished completely. It was as though a heavy fog had been lifted. The thick, oppressive weariness clinging to me evaporated instantly. It left my body light and invigorated.  

In truth, I almost collapsed in the same euphoric state as Maristel. But I clenched my abs and kept myself grounded—barely. It’s my little secret. Well done, me.  

“…Wow, this is incredible. Potions work this well?”  

It even cured my stiff shoulders. I rotated them experimentally while addressing Isezaki-san.  

Before she could respond, Maristel pouted and answered in her stead.  

“No, no. This isn’t just any potion. This is something much more exceptional. If you sprinkle this on a wound, even severe injuries will heal instantly. It’s the kind of thing that’s too valuable to drink. Isezaki, this must be… a High Potion, isn’t it?”  

“I wouldn’t know… This is my first time making one. But judging by your reaction, it’s probably that level of quality…”  

“Your *first time* making one, huh…”  

Maristel gave Isezaki-san a half-lidded, exasperated stare as she averted her gaze.  

“For one thing, no matter how carefully you make it, you shouldn’t be able to create something of this caliber from Healer’s Herb in the first place. Hey, hey, Isezaki, how did you manage to whip this up so easily!? My understanding of alchemy is falling apart here!”  

Maristel flailed her arms like a child throwing a tantrum. Watching her, Isezaki-san awkwardly played with her hair as she answered.  

“I-I’m sorry… You seemed so determined, so I couldn’t bring myself to say anything…”  

“Hmph, I’ll let it slide. After all, when you create something like this, it’s a case of ‘No words are needed for the defeated sage’.”  

Maristel puffed out her cheeks and turned her head away with a huff. It seemed like she was referring to something akin to “the howl of the defeated dog” or “a defeated commander should not explain himself.”  

It made sense. With how earnest she had been, it would’ve been hard for Isezaki-san to speak up. Finally, I understood why she’d seemed so uneasy earlier.  

Having gotten her frustrations out, Maristel stood abruptly, brushed off her skirt, and stared at both me and Isezaki-san with scrutinizing eyes.  

“Still… you two are really something else, huh? You’re like a pair of absurd, out-of-this-world creatures. Maybe that’s the kind of thing you need to get close to nobility. …Though, that beast tamer wasn’t all that impressive. And even they were connected to nobility, so maybe not?”  

“Huh? The beast tamer? You mean the Earth Dragon’s…? You’ve met him before?”  

“I just remembered. You know those golem talismans we picked up? After staring at them over and over, it finally came back to me.”  

Maristel pulled one of the talismans from her bag—the same ones we had found embedded in the golems.  

“Beast tamers have a unique crest engraved on the back of their hands, and they replicate that crest onto their talismans. The beast tamer I once met had this exact same crest on his hand. I ran into him at a dark guild—”  

“Um, what’s a dark guild?”  

“Ugh, don’t interrupt! …It’s like a shady broker for risky jobs. The one I frequented looked like nothing more than a rundown tavern.”  

“S-sorry…”  

“Anyway, it was about a year ago. I went there looking for work, and I saw a beast tamer drunk and in high spirits. He was slurring about how he was ‘different from the rest of us’, and how ‘this big upcoming job has a huge payout’. I was jealous and eavesdropped nearby. He mentioned working with the Digram family or something like that. Nobody believed him at the time—it sounded far-fetched—but now that I think about it…”  

“The Digram family?”  

“That’s right.”  

I glanced at Isezaki-san, who gave a small nod.  

The beast tamer… He was the one responsible for the assassination attempt on Lady Levia. While I had suspected that the mastermind was her sister, Delixir, could this mean that the neighboring Digram family had also been involved in the plot?  

But wait… the Digram family had severed ties with Delixir after her engagement to their heir fell through. That was why they had no qualms about launching an invasion into the Carius territory’s Grandain region…  

“Husband, it might be wise to inform Lady Levia about this.”

“Y-yeah, you’re right. Um, Maristel, could I have one of those talismans?”  

“Sure, take one.”  

I took a talisman from her. There was still a chance this could all be a coincidence. I hadn’t thoroughly examined the beast tamer’s corpse. But Holly had conducted a detailed investigation. She should remember if there had been a crest on their hand and what it looked like.  

Just when I thought things had settled down with Lady Levia, yet another complication had arisen.  

Even though my body had been refreshed by the potion, I felt a heavy weight settle in my stomach. I let out a deep sigh and looked up at the ceiling.

+++

# 210. Night's Anticipation

『Levia’s older sister, Delixir, might be colluding with the Digram family—』

The underground room fell into a heavy silence after receiving this stomach-churning piece of information from Maristel. It was Maristel herself who eventually broke the quiet.  

“What’s with those faces~? Don’t tell me that was a big deal of information or something? If it is, you better mention my name to the nobles and give me some credit. I’d love a reward or two~.”  

“You’re the informant, so of course, your name will be mentioned. I can’t promise you any rewards, though.”  

“Mufufu~ I’ll count on you then. …Well, that’s that for this topic—”  

Maristel twisted her waist playfully and looked up at us with a sly gaze.  

“So, what next…? Should we chat until we get sleepy? Or just go to bed already? I’m fine either way~.”  

“Oh, right. About sleeping arrangements—how’s that going to work? There’s a bed upstairs, but that’s yours, isn’t it, Maristel?”  

“Yep. But it’s pretty big, so there’s no problem if three people share it~♡.”  

“Three peo—! That’s completely out of the question. Husband!”  

“Ah, yeah, you’re right. Maristel, sorry, but we’ll have to decline that.”  

“Oh dear, such a shame. In that case, I’ll sleep here, so you two can use the bed upstairs.”  

“…….You’re sleeping here, Maristel?”  

“Yep. When I get absorbed in my research, I often just sleep down here instead of going back up. Don’t worry about it~.”  

She gestured towards a large sofa. Indeed, it was spacious enough for someone to lie down comfortably.  

“In that case, I’ll sleep here, and Maristel and Isezaki can use the bed upstairs—”  

“N-no way, Master! Don’t make me sleep with ***her***!”  

“How rude~. Didn’t I tell you already? I’m not interested in women.”  

“Like I’d believe a word you say!”  

“Ugh, but it’s true~.”  

It seemed like Isezaki-san and Maristel had grown a bit closer. But the tension between them returned almost instantly. Still, it felt less sharp than before.  

“Well, if Isezaki insists… Maristel, sorry to trouble you, but we’ll take the bed upstairs.”  

“Sure thing. I’ll just keep researching these magic talismans until I get sleepy and crash here. You two can relax upstairs~♪.”  

Maristel casually dumped a bag full of magical talismans onto the desk, waving her hand lazily without turning around. That seemed to signal the end of the conversation. It was surprisingly straightforward, but that was fine.  

“Alright then, let’s head back upstairs.”  

“Y-yes. Husband…! T-to share a bed with Husband… sharing a bed with… with Husband…”  

Isezaki muttered under her breath, her face burning bright red. Feeling her nervousness and unease, I said nothing and quietly climbed the stairs.  

◇◇◇  

“_Grind-grind, grind-grind_♡… _Grind-grind, grind-grind_♡… Ahaha, Sleep Aroma’s complete~♪”  

After shaping the freshly made _Sleep Aroma_ on a plate, I decided to set my plan into motion.  

Barefoot to avoid making noise, I carefully climbed the stone stairs step by step, carrying the plate in one hand.  

My objective, of course, was… a **midnight visit**♡.  

The annoying Isezaki would be put to deep sleep with the Sleep Aroma. And during that blissful quiet, I’d have Matsunaga all to myself♪.  

Unable to contain my excitement, I started shedding clothes one by one as I ascended the stairs. Before I knew it—oh my—there I was, in the nude.  

Ufufu, my body is just so beautiful, seductive, graceful, and elegant… enchanting and mysterious, with a refined allure. No man could resist this figure.  

But Matsunaga… he only glances at me from time to time, never making a move.  

Well, that cool, distant attitude is something I like about him for now♡.  

But tonight is different. If he keeps holding back like this, I might lose my mind from all the teasing.

+++

# 211. Reporting, Communication, Consultation

“—[Dimensional Teleport].”  

Leaving behind a written note, Isezaki-san and I teleported from Maristel’s house using [Dimensional Teleport].  

Considering that Maristel would likely attempt something inappropriate during the night, I had been mulling over what to do. Fortunately, some timely information gave me an excuse to act.  

This plan allowed us to move under the cover of night without raising suspicion, which was another bonus. While there was a chance Maristel didn’t intend anything mischievous, I couldn’t be sure. If she didn’t, I’d hope she takes this as a chance to reflect on her behavior.  

Our destination was, of course, my personal room within Lady Levia’s castle.  

The outside was pitch dark, though it wasn’t yet late enough for bedtime. After reporting the necessary information, I intended to spend the night here.  

In the faint glow of the magical night lamp that dimly illuminated the room—  

“O-o-overnight… bed… together…”  

A faint murmur reached my ears from beside me.  

It was, of course, Isezaki-san. Her vacant gaze stared into the void as she muttered incoherently.  

This stemmed from an earlier incident when we parted ways with Maristel.  

As soon as Isezaki-san entered Maristel’s bedroom, she had been visibly flustered, her eyes darting wildly as she exclaimed:  

_‘Huff! Huff! Huff! Eheh, we’re married, so of course, we’ll share the same bed, right? Yes, naturally! I get it, I understand completely! And surely, Maristel will come to check on us later! So, let’s act like a married couple and, um, maybe try an… an arm pillow? Showing her a lovey-dovey scene will definitely fool her! We could even try hugging while sleeping—that would work perfectly! I-I’m an expert on married couples, after all!’_  

She had rattled this off with increasing fervor, smacking the bed repeatedly for emphasis. An expert on married couples? Isezaki-san wasn’t even married herself.  

Even though she had been in such a frantic state, after I suggested returning via [Dimensional Teleport], she seemed to lose all spirit. When I asked her to draft the note, she was clearly elsewhere mentally. It led to her current state of complete disengagement.  

I guessed she had steeled herself for her role as a fake wife, only to be thrown off balance when that preparation went unused. It seemed a little pitiful. But there was no way I could share a bed with the landlady’s precious daughter. Even without teleportation, I would have found a way to avoid it.  

I addressed Isezaki-san, whose vacant expression remained unchanged.  

“Um… Isezaki-san? We’ve arrived. Are you okay?”  

“Ah! Husband’s voice! Huh, where is this? I… I am… your wife, Isezaki!”  

“This is my room in Lady Levia’s castle. You don’t need to pretend to be my wife here.”  

“Oh, that’s right…! I-I’m sorry, I seem to have gotten a bit confused…”  

“Good to hear you’re alright. Shall I call for Holly now?”  

“Y-yes! I’m so sorry for the trouble…”  

It seemed she had returned to her senses. Although Isezaki-san was fidgeting with her hair in embarrassment, I had grown accustomed to her strange behavior. I decided to let it slide and moved to switch the night lamp to a brighter setting before ringing the bell.  

◇◇◇

Holly arrived promptly. And after explaining the situation, she led us to a reception room.  

We waited for a while in the reception room until Holly returned, accompanied by Lady Levia herself.  

“Matsunaga, may I see that magic talisman you mentioned earlier?”  

I handed over the talisman, and Holly furrowed her brow as she examined it.  

“There’s no mistaking it. This is indeed the emblem engraved on that summoner’s hand. It seems they were an agent of the Digram family.”  

“I thought my sister was foolish, but to think she’s connected to the Digram family…”  

Lady Levia muttered as she massaged her temples. It seemed even she hadn’t foreseen this possibility.  

“Um, Lady Levia, don’t you think this has gone a bit too far? Perhaps you should consult your father about this?”  

To begin with, the idea of an older sister trying to assassinate her younger sister was already outrageous. But for a daughter to conspire with a rival noble family? Surely, as the head of the family, her father couldn’t overlook such a matter.  

However, Lady Levia shrugged and replied, 

“My father adores my sister to the point of obsession. He wouldn’t believe a word I say. On the contrary, if I were to travel to the capital for an explanation or report, my sister would likely seize the opportunity to eliminate me for good. Even now—”  

Lady Levia reached into her pocket and tossed a handful of letters onto the table.

“These are all summons demanding I resign as the overseer of Grandain and return to the capital. Of course, I’ve been refusing, citing administrative duties. But it’s clear they are desperate to get me within their reach. Oh ho ho…”  

She laughed faintly, the sound devoid of strength.  

Isezaki-san gently placed a comforting hand on her shoulder. 

“Levi, I’ve told you many times before: if you asked my grandmother, she could arrange for you and those close to you to get registered in Japan. You could live there and—”  

“Dear sister, it’s a very tempting offer. But I’ll be fine. If anything, this is where the real battle begins.”  

Lady Levia grasped Isezaki-san’s hand and shook her head.  

“Originally, I intended to make further progress on the redevelopment of the magic stone mines before taking action… But if my sister is colluding with the Digram family, I can’t afford to wait any longer.”  

“……….Levi, what exactly are you planning to do?”  

At Isezaki-san’s question, Lady Levia stood tall, puffed out her chest, and declared boldly,  

“I, Levia Carius, will pledge to King Melcheria of the Kingdom of Revis to continue the development and prosperity of the magic stone mines. With the results of this work as my foundation, I intend to formally request the independence of Grandain and its surrounding magic stone mines, establishing them as the independent territory of Levia!”  

With that, she made an unexpected proclamation of independence.

+++

# 212. Declaration of Independence

“Independence…? Is that even possible?”  

I asked skeptically, and Holly immediately answered without hesitation.  

“In the Kingdom of Revis, there have been numerous instances of land division or transfer since its founding. For example, in the western Murrent County, a succession dispute led to the territory being split between the eldest and second sons. In the southern Southrail Viscounty, part of the land was confiscated as punishment for the viscount’s misconduct and subsequently transferred to a noble who resolved the matter. In the central region, there was also—”  

“Okay, okay, I get it. That’s enough…”  

Apparently, there were plenty of precedents for such cases. It wasn’t some idea she’d just come up with on a whim—Lady Levia must have been seriously considering independence for a while. Still, the scale of this situation suddenly felt massive.  

“But Levi….If you go through with this independence and fail…”  

“Yes, Sister. If independence isn’t recognized, my sister and father will accuse me of rebellion, and… well, most likely, I’d face execution by beheading. However, if I do nothing, the same fate awaits me sooner or later. In that case, I must act. And for that, I will… do whatever it takes!”  

Lady Levia declared this resolutely, her determined gaze somehow directed at me.  

“Uh, why are you looking at me like that?”  

“Matsunaga-sama, should the Levia Territory be acknowledged, I promise to grant you an appropriate—or, no, even greater—position and power of your choosing. So, would you please lend me your strength?”  

“I don’t need power or status, not even a sliver.”  

No, thank you. I’d said as much to Lady Levia before, but I guess nobles find it hard to comprehend. She widened her eyes, looking genuinely astonished as if thinking, “What? You don’t want power or status? Really?”  

“Levi, it’s impossible for Uncle to work under someone and abide by their whims. After all, what Uncle truly seeks is to live freely, untethered by anything, following his heart. Someone like that would never desire such worldly things as power or status, right, Uncle?”  

“Ah, well, yeah. That’s… accurate.”  

Isezaki-san passionately argued her point with sparkling eyes. It felt exaggerated, but not entirely wrong.  

“I see… In that case, how about becoming my husband, Matsunaga-sama? Despite appearances, I’m a diligent worker and a very devoted woman. If we were to marry, I could guarantee you a life of luxury—Eek!”  

Lady Levia’s confident tone faltered as her face turned pale.  

“J-just kidding! A noble’s marriage isn’t something decided on the spur of the moment! My apologies for the slip! Oh ho ho ho ho ho ho!”  

For some reason, Lady Levia glanced nervously at Isezaki-san as she awkwardly laughed. Well, not that I intended to entertain this conversation further—I wasn’t looking to become a kept man. Besides, more importantly—  

“Lady Levia, I don’t need any rewards. If it’s within my ability, I’ll help you. So for now, can you tell me the details of your plan?”  

“Oh my! Oh my, my, my! Really? Thank you, Matsunaga-sama!”  

“…..Are you sure about this, Uncle?”  

Lady Levia looked ecstatic, practically leaping out of her seat with joy. While Isezaki-san, in stark contrast, furrowed her brows in concern. I gave her a reassuring nod.  

“Yeah. You know, when we went herb-gathering, it made me realize how important connections are in this world. Thanks to that, we got into the mines without any tedious procedures. If I’m going to keep visiting this world, earning Lady Levia’s goodwill isn’t a bad move.”  

With noble privilege, I’d easily gained access to the magic stone mines and quickly gathered a large haul of herbs. The benefits of leveraging aristocratic power in this feudal society weren’t lost on me.  

“…Besides, Isezaki-san, I know how much you care about Lady Levia. For your sake, I want to help her.”  

Ultimately, this was my biggest motivation.  

For the sake of Isezaki-san, who cherished Lady Levia—a childhood friend from this world, practically a sister—I was willing to go the extra mile.  

“Uncle…”  

Isezaki-san looked at me with tearful eyes. Feeling a bit embarrassed, I quickly redirected the conversation to Lady Levia.  

“…So, Lady Levia, what exactly do you want me to do?”  

“Ah, yes… Before that, I’d like to ask you something. How is your potion-making progressing?”  

“Huh? Oh, well, thanks to Lady Levia’s connections and Isezaki-san’s magic, we’ve made good progress on that front—”  

“Don’t forget that Uncle showcased his exceptional skills by exterminating the monsters lurking in the mines!”  

“Haha, well, yeah, things are going smoothly for now. All that’s left is selling them in Japan.”  

“I see. If I recall correctly, a single day in Japan corresponds to three days here, right?”  

“Yes, that’s right. Lately, the time ratio has been stable at that level.”  

Originally, the difference was ten days. But since my magical power leveled up, it’s been fixed at three days.  

“I see… Then, as long as you spend most of your time in Japan, would you mind transporting the gathered supplies to the magic stone mines every two days?”  

“If it’s just that, I don’t mind… Is that really all you want me to do?”  

Transporting supplies wasn’t much of a task; I had already done it today as a side job. It felt almost too simple, like an anticlimax.  

“Matsunaga-sama, this is a critical mission. Right now, our top priority is to send a large amount of supplies to advance the development of the magic stone mines. Without restarting the mining operations, the notion of independence won’t even be entertained.”  

“That’s true… You can’t present independence to the king without any tangible results to back it up.”  

“So, I’ll transport supplies here every two days and spend the rest of my time in Japan. That’s fine, right?”  

“Yes. It also takes time to gather the materials in Grandain. So that schedule should work perfectly.”  

That arrangement worked well for me too since I could also focus on potion sales in Japan.  

“Got it. _Whew_… Having you formally ask for my help made me think it would be something much harder, haha.”  

I sighed in relief, rolling my shoulders to ease the tension that had unknowingly built up. Then, Isezaki-san leaned in, pointing her index finger at me with a serious expression.  

“Uncle, as she said, this is a very significant task. Instantly transporting goods from one place to another? It’s like you alone are controlling the logistics of this entire world. Especially here, the implications are enormous. Your decisions could impact the power dynamics of various countries and territories. In essence, Uncle, you wield influence akin to ruling the world itself… As expected of you, Uncle!”  

“No, no, that’s definitely an overstatement…”  

I’m just a glorified delivery guy.  

“By the way, Matsunaga-sama. You plan to sell the potions to wealthy individuals in Japan, correct?”  

“Yes, that’s the idea. Potions are even rarer there than here, so I intend to sell them at a high price to affluent buyers.”  

Hearing my response, Lady Levia rested her chin on her hand and fell silent for a moment, deep in thought.  

“Hmm… Then I have one suggestion—or rather, a request—for you.”  

“What is it?”  

“Until the supply transport is completed, would you allow Colin to serve as your bodyguard while you’re in Japan?”  

“Huh? Colin? As my bodyguard?”  

At Lady Levia’s unexpected request, I could only tilt my head in confusion.

+++

# 213. Violation of Labor Standards Law

“Huh? A bodyguard? No, no, that’s overkill! As you know, Lady Levia, there’s no magic in Japan, nor are there monsters. Compared to this world, it’s incredibly safe!”  

“Are you absolutely certain of that? Automobiles, escalators… Japan seemed to me to have many dangerous things.”  

While automobiles might be understandable, escalators? …Really? That one feels like it’s just Lady Levia. I couldn’t outright say that, so my face stiffened awkwardly as she continued.  

“Not to mention pick-up artists, door-to-door salesmen, gropers, peeping Toms, complainers, bump-into-you old men, and scalpers—so many kinds of outlaws! I heard about them from Lady Aihara. I’m truly worried about you, Matsunaga-sama.”  

It seems Aihara, who has picked up some of the local language, had been chatting with Lady Levia. That’s fine and all, but I wish she wouldn’t put weird ideas in her head.  

“If something were to happen to you, Matsunaga-sama, this entire plan would collapse. I fully understand that this is a selfish request on my part. But please, I beg of you, allow Colin to act as your bodyguard!”  

Lady Levia looked at me with earnest eyes. She was serious. If that’s the case, I figured I should ask for Isezaki-san’s opinion as well.  

“Isezaki-san, what do you think?”  

“Of course, I believe Uncle could handle any danger that comes his way. But Levia’s understanding of Uncle is still quite… ‘shallow,’ you see. I can understand her desire to ensure everything is perfectly prepared. Ah, new members always lack perspective, don’t they? Hehe…”  

Isezaki-san laughed to herself, speaking in an oddly condescending tone.  

Shallow, deep, new, veteran—whatever. The fact is, having a key figure in this mission wandering around not only in an unreachable place but in another world might understandably make people nervous. For Lady Levia, this was a critical moment.  

Given that I had agreed to cooperate, I wanted to ease her worries, but—  

“I understand that Lady Levia is concerned for my safety. But… asking Colin to take on such a role feels a bit much…”  

I knew very well how strong Colin was.  

However, having someone as young as Colin act as a bodyguard didn’t sit right with me. In this world, sure, but in Japan? She’d be considered elementary school age. The Labor Standards Law crossed my mind.  

If anything, I’d prefer Holly—though she’s Lady Levia’s secretary and bodyguard, so she’s probably not available.  

I glanced at Holly. Suddenly, she spoke up.  

“Then how about we ask Colin directly? Colin, you’re listening, aren’t you?”  

Holly called out toward the door behind us. A startled “Eek!” came from the other side, followed by the slow opening of the door. Colin peeked in hesitantly, with Aihara trailing nervously behind her.  

“I-I’m sorry…”  

“Holly-san! Colin-chan not bad! Me told her ‘Let’s go see!’ okay?”  

Aihara defended Colin in broken language. Holly sighed and fixed her gaze on Colin.  

“Colin… Even if Lady Aihara suggested it, your position requires you to discourage such actions. I’ll address this issue thoroughly later. For now, come in.”  

“Yes, ma’am…”  

“Y-yes…”  

The two entered the room, shoulders slumped in dejection.  

“Colin, as you overheard, Lady Levia wishes for you to act as Matsunaga-sama’s bodyguard in Japan. Setting aside that this is an order, let me ask: what do you want to do?”  

“I want to go! I want to go! Lady Aihara said Japan sounds super interesting! I’ll be a bodyguard or whatever it takes—I just want to see it, Sis!”  

Colin responded eagerly, her excitement overflowing. By the end, her usual little-sister personality peeked through.  

“Refer to me as ‘Head Maid,’ not ‘Big Sister.’ And this isn’t a sightseeing trip; it’s to protect Matsunaga-sama. Do you understand that?”  

“Of course, Head Maid!”  

With a crisp, energetic reply, Colin straightened her back confidently. Then Aihara stepped up to me, clasping her hands together with a pleading expression.  

“Senpai, please! I owe Colin-chan so much for helping me out. I really want to return the favor while we’re over there. I’ll pitch in and help, so please take her along!”  

Now that she mentioned it, I had completely relied on Colin to handle Aihara’s sightseeing in this world. That must have been quite a hassle for Colin (definitely).  

Leaving things without properly thanking her didn’t feel right—especially as an adult.  

Well… it wouldn’t be for too long. And if I thought of it as a kind of homestay, taking Colin along might not be so bad. Even if the “bodyguard” aspect wasn’t entirely serious.  

“All right… In that case, Colin-chan, would you come with me to Japan?”  

The moment I said that, Colin’s face lit up with a brilliant smile. Then, she exclaimed with an enthusiastic—  

“Thank you so much! I’ll do my absolute best to live up to your expectations, Matsunaga-sama! Looking forward to working with you☆!”  

“………..Wait, Japanese?!”  

I was stunned speechless, but Aihara leaned in with a smug expression.  

“Pretty awesome, right? While she was teaching me this world’s language, Colin-chan ended up mastering Japanese before I even got the hang of it!”  

“You’re kidding…”  

Now that I thought about it, she had cracked the Stinger’s hand signals instantly and started using them effortlessly. But mastering Japanese in a day? That’s beyond genius-level prodigy.  

The only drawback was that her Japanese had a faint “Aihara-ish” customization to it. But if Aihara was her teacher, I couldn’t really complain. Actually, it might even help her blend in better in Japan.  

And so, with our genius prodigy in tow, we began our return to Japan.

+++

# 214. An Overnight Stay

As planned, we spent the night at the castle that day.  

I relaxed alone in my assigned room. While Lady Levia, under the pretext of preparing for the critical moment ahead, apparently enjoyed a pajama party with Isezaki-san and the others.  

The next morning—  

“Colin, be sure to protect Matsunaga-sama well.”  

“Yep! I’ll do my best, Sis!”  

“Call me Head Maid. …Matsunaga-sama. I believe she may be lacking in some ways, but please use Colin as your shield if necessary.”  

Holly bowed deeply, her sincerity palpable. Beside her, Lady Levia pinched the hem of her skirt and gave an elegant curtsy.  

“Then, two days from now—six days by my reckoning—I eagerly look forward to seeing you again.”  

“Yes, I’ll make sure to return. …All right, shall we go?”  

I extended my hand, and Isezaki-san took my right while Aihara took my left. Colin, looking a bit lost, glanced around awkwardly.  

“Ah, sorry. It looks like I’m out of hands. Hmm, Isezaki-san and Aihara, could you two hold Colin-chan’s hands instead?”  

“Like this?”  

“Sure thing!”  

With the two of them holding Colin’s hands, the four of us formed a circle reminiscent of summoning a UFO.  

I’d never performed [Dimensional Teleport] in such a formation. But as long as I could visualize it, the spell should work fine. After all, magic relies heavily on imagination.  

“Excuse me, then. —[Dimensional Teleport].”  

◇◇◇  

In the blink of an eye, we arrived at the entrance of Haruna Apartments: Matsunaga Koutarou’s Residence—my home.  

Even though it had only been a one-night stay in the other world, it felt like ages since I’d last been home. It was likely because of how eventful the day had been.  

“Wow! So this is… Japan?!”  

Colin’s voice was brimming with excitement as she took in her surroundings with wide eyes. It seemed the teleportation had succeeded without any issues, thankfully.  

“Yep, this is my place in Japan.”  

“Colin-chan, welcome to Japan~! Woohoo!”  

“Woohoo, Lady Aihara!”  

**_Clap!_**

Aihara and Colin high-fived enthusiastically.  

“Uh, Matsunaga-sama! May I explore this house a bit?!”  

Deciding to stick to Japanese while she was here, Colin immediately adopted a casual tone as she asked excitedly.  

“Sure, go ahead and look around. There’s not much interesting here. But if that’s fine with you, explore to your heart’s content.”  

“Seriously?! Then I’m going exploring too!”  

“Wait for me, Lady Aihara~!”  

Aihara responded even before Colin, and the young girl eagerly mimicked her. She slipped off her shoes at the entrance and rushed after Aihara into the apartment with loud footsteps.  

This left just me and Isezaki-san behind.  

“Not going with them, Isezaki-san?”  

“Hehe… No need. At this point, this place feels like a second home to me.”  

Really? I doubted that, but I chose not to comment.  

Isezaki-san stood calmly with her arms crossed. She was watching the young girl and woman bustling about my cramped apartment. It seemed her “seniority” attitude from yesterday still lingered.  

However, her composure wavered as Aihara ventured into my bedroom.  

“Oh, found Senpai’s bed~! Let’s check under it, just in case. What treasures might be hidden here?”  

“Lady Aihara, is there something special under the bed?”  

“Hehe, this is where the real treasures are hidden!”  

“Treasures?! That’s amazing!”  

“All right, time to investigate Senpai’s preferences!”  

“R-Rio-san, wait for me! For, uh, educational purposes!”  

At that, Isezaki-san raised her voice and hurriedly charged into the room. As a young woman herself, she must have felt a twinge of desire to join in the fun.  

For the record, there was nothing incriminating under my bed. Any questionable material was safely stored on my computer.  

And so, I stood in the background. With my arms crossed, I observed the three women giggling and playing in my home.  

◇◇◇  

“Alright, now that things have settled down, let’s talk about what’s next,” 

I said, addressing the three as we sat around the table.  

Isezaki-san and Aihara sipped their coffee. While Colin, with her milk in hand, looked at me expectantly.  

“First off, Aihara. I need you to distribute potions to the VIP ward. You’re up for that, right?”  

“Of course! That’s part of why I asked for the isekai tour deal in the first place. Honestly, handing out medicine to some old folks is so easy it doesn’t even feel like fair compensation. Are you sure this is all you wanted?”  

“Absolutely. If I were the one distributing them, it’d seem suspicious. And they might not accept the potions. This arrangement is perfect. So, when can you do it?”  

“Hmm, right now works. It’s lunchtime, and the weather’s nice. The old folks are probably out in the spacious lobby soaking up the sun. I’d have my pick of the bunch.”  

“Really? Then can I ask you to go right away?”  

“Sure, but what about you, Senpai?”  

“Let’s see… I could tag along. If I plan to sell potions in the future, it might be good to get my face known.”  

“Yes! If Matsunaga-sama is going, I’m coming too! I’m your bodyguard, after all!”  

“Me too, of course!” 

Isezaki-san chimed in, raising her hand eagerly alongside Colin.  

But that was going to be a problem.  

“Uh, no. Let’s not do that.”  

“But I want to be useful to you, Uncle!” 

Isezaki-san said, clenching her fists and showing her determination.  

She wanted to repay me for helping Lady Levia, and I understood her sentiment completely. But taking a big group to the hospital lobby would only draw unnecessary attention and suspicion.  

“In that case… Isezaki-san, could I ask you to show Colin around instead? Colin-chan still needs to get used to Japan before she can properly act as a bodyguard, don’t you think?”  

Isezaki-san exhaled sharply, her enthusiasm undeterred.  

“Understood! Leave Colin-chan to me!”  

Colin seemed equally agreeable.  

“Got it! I’ll start by getting used to Japan. Isezaki-sama, first, let me see those *automobile* and *escalators* Lady Levia mentioned. I’ll take them down with one punch!” 

“Uh, r-right. Yes, Colin-chan, let’s start by learning about those things…” 

Isezaki-san replied, looking troubled.  

Yeah, Colin’s education was in her hands now.  

“Alright, that wraps things up for now. If anything comes up, just contact me via smartphone.”

“Understood, Uncle. Well then, Colin-chan, shall we head out?”  

“Okay! Cars! Escalators! Creepy flirty guys! Clumsy old men! Scalpers! Bring it on!”  

“Uh, Colin-chan, you shouldn’t yell things like that in public…”  

For a while after that, I tended to some errands. Eventually, Isezaki-san and Colin left the house, leaving the place quiet. It was just me and Aihara now.  

She slid closer to me, her cheeks slightly flushed. And she looked up at me with a sly grin.  

“Hehe, Senpai. Just the two of us now…♡”  ‘

“Yeah, so let’s get going.”  

“Aww, Senpai, you’re no fun!”  

Ignoring her pout, I firmly grabbed Aihara’s hand and teleported us straight to Juuzou-san’s hospital room with [Dimensional Teleport].

+++

# 215. Business Begins

“Ah, there you are, Rio and Matsunaga-kun. I’ve been waiting for you.”  

Using [Dimensional Teleport], we arrived at the VIP ward in the hospital room belonging to Rio’s grandfather, Jounai Juuzou.  

The room didn’t resemble a hospital room at all—it was luxurious, almost extravagant. Juuzou greeted us with a warm smile as we entered.  

“Sorry for the trouble, Juuzou-san, and for using your room like this…”  

Initially, I’d planned to teleport somewhere near the hospital instead of barging into Juuzou’s room. But Rio had gone ahead and called her grandfather on her smartphone, saying, “Why not just use Grandpa’s room?” before I could stop her. Considering this was unrelated to Juuzou, I felt a little guilty.  

“Haha, don’t worry about such small things. Feel free to use it anytime. But more importantly, the potion you mentioned—the one from the other world—were you able to procure it?”  

“Yes. Rather than ‘procure,’ we gathered the ingredients. And I had Isezaki-san prepare it.”  

“Oh, Seina-chan made it? Excellent. Could I take a look at it?”  

“Oh, nice, Grandpa! I haven’t seen it yet either, so this’ll be fun.”  

“If you’d like, why not try drinking some? It’s the same potion we’re about to distribute, after all.”  

“Really? Then please, let me try it.”  

“Me too, me too!”  

I poured the potion—carried in a plastic bottle—into glasses prepared by Juuzou’s staff.  

Juuzou and Rio both picked up their glasses, carefully observing the potion’s contents. Perhaps because they were family, their curious mannerisms were oddly similar.  

“Hmm… It looks just like water.”  

“Yeah, no particular smell either~”  

“This is diluted, but the undiluted version glows faintly.”  

Using the undiluted High Potion as-is would’ve been too potent. To avoid causing a commotion while distributing them in the lobby, we watered it down, turning it into a high-quality regular potion. This should be much more manageable, according to Isezaki-san.  

“I see. Well, here goes.”  

“Alrighty, bottoms up!”  

Juuzou and Rio tilted their glasses back, finishing the potion in one gulp. It was quite a sight.  

Afterward, they both seemed to reflect on how they felt, placing a hand on their chests or exhaling lightly. Juuzou spoke first.  

“Hmm… My body feels warm, and I feel very refreshed.”  

“The taste is kinda like bitter water, but it’s refreshing and feels amazing? Like, super chill vibes—this is wild!”  

While their impressions differed, they both seemed pleased.  

Incidentally, the potion can easily cure issues like stiffness, headaches, and chronic fatigue. Since neither mentioned feeling significantly better, it seemed they were both already in good health.  

“Alright then, we’ll be heading to the lobby to distribute these. Rio, let’s go.”  

“Got it. See you later, Grandpa!”  

“Hmm. Rio, you know what to do…”  

“Yeah, yeah. I’ll be careful about who I give the potions to. So don’t worry, Grandpa.”  

“Hmm? Rio, what does he mean?”  

“Oh, this ward is full of wealthy people. So, you know, there’s always some quirky characters around. But don’t worry—my grandma and grandpa’s friends are all cool!”  

I see. That made sense. If you’re in the VIP ward, you’ve got enough money to turn heads and likely a personality to match. If I wasn’t careful, even minor comments could spark trouble.  

……For now, I figured it was best to leave things to Rio and keep myself as inconspicuous as possible. Not that I was scared or anything—but, yeah, better safe than sorry.  

With my resolve steeled, I left Juuzou’s room alongside Rio.  

◇◇◇

When I sold monster meat to Juuzou, I always teleported directly to his room. So visiting the lobby again felt fresh.  

The high-class furnishings and serene atmosphere still gave it the feel of a luxury hotel or resort rather than a hospital.  

In the center of the lobby was a Japanese garden. Sunlight illuminated the pine trees swaying gently in the wind, while koi swam leisurely in a pond. A pond and koi fish… in a hospital? Yeah, this place really was out of the ordinary.  

The lobby bustled more than I remembered, likely due to Rio’s claim that it was an active time of day.  

As we walked across the plush carpet, a portly old man and a stylish middle-aged woman approached from the opposite direction. However, Rio didn’t seem inclined to speak to them. So I guessed they didn’t meet her criteria for potion recipients.  

The elderly man bore a striking resemblance to a retired politician I used to see often on TV. But it was probably just my imagination. Meanwhile, the woman accompanying him wore a bold, shoulder-revealing top and clung to him closely.  

Now that I think about it, Juuzou once mentioned that this ward was sometimes used by people hiding from the public or bringing in their mistresses. Could that elderly man be one of them?  

Then again, it’s perfectly normal for children or grandchildren to visit their family in the hospital. Maybe she’s just a granddaughter doting on her grandpa. As I chastised myself for being judgmental, I saw the old man casually fondling the woman’s backside as they passed by.  

……..Well, I guess I wasn’t entirely wrong.  

With that amusing observation, I followed Rio while taking in the lively atmosphere of the lobby. She seemed to be heading directly toward the central courtyard.  

By the pond in the courtyard, a lone elderly man sat on a bench. Rio tugged on my sleeve.  

“Senpai, that old guy is someone I know.”  

“Really? Who is he?”  

“He used to work for the Jounai Group and was kinda like Grandpa’s right-hand man back in the day. Wanna go chat with him for a bit?”  

Apparently, he was one of Juuzou’s former confidants. Since he was someone Juuzou knew, it would likely make things easier for me as well.  

We entered the garden and approached the elderly man.  

At first glance, it seemed like he was watching the koi in the pond. But as we got closer, it became clear he wasn’t looking at the koi—just staring blankly into space. The sight was honestly a bit concerning.  

I glanced at Rio, who whispered with a resigned look, 

“Yeah, he’s been like this a lot lately.”  

The crunch of gravel under our feet seemed to stir the man from his stupor. His shoulders moved slightly, and he turned his face toward us.  

“Oh… Rio-chan. Visiting Juuzou again today?”  

“Yep, and while I’m at it, I’m visiting you too, Grandpa Shuuji!”  

“Haha, so I’m an afterthought? I’m still happy to see you, of course. And who’s this young man?”  

He shifted his gaze to me for the first time. The man was gaunt, his body and face emaciated, almost skeletal. But his eyes were sharp, like a blade. His piercing gaze made me hold my breath for a moment.  

“Uh, nice to meet you. I’m Matsunaga Koutarou. I used to work with her at the same company.”  

“I see. But why would someone like you be here? You should know this isn’t a place you can visit out of mere curiosity. I’d suggest leaving before you cause any trouble.”  

He frowned and scrutinized me with suspicion. Before I could respond, Rio stepped between us with an exaggerated sigh of exasperation.  

“Ughhh, Grandpa Shuuji, you’re as grumpy as ever! Senpai knows Grandpa too, okay? So it’s not weird for him to be here!”  

“He knows Juuzou? …I see. That old man’s been getting healthier lately. Is he planning to come out of retirement and start some new venture?”  

“Nope, not that either! Senpai’s like… Grandpa’s friend! Right, Senpai?”  

“Uh, haha, yeah… something like that.”  

I wasn’t exactly Juuzou’s *friend*, but explaining our business relationship would only complicate things further. I decided to just smile and nod.  

“His friend… I see. My apologies. It was improper of me to question someone Rio-chan and Juuzou know.”  

With that, the man—Souda Shuuji—gave a slight bow.  

“Matsunaga-san, forgive me. It’s an old habit from my working days. I can’t help but be wary of unfamiliar faces. Please, think of it as the ramblings of an old man and let it slide. I’m Souda Shuuji, just an elderly man waiting for the end of his days.”  

“Hey, hey, enough with the gloomy talk. Are you feeling worse lately or something?”  

“Well, my cancer has progressed to a later stage. Palliative care can only do so much. But unlike Juuzou, I don’t have close family ties to complicate things. So it’s not all bad.”  

Leaning back on the bench, Souda gave a faint, weary laugh.  

“Come on, Grandpa Shuuji! Stop with the depressing stuff! You’ve gotta live longer!”  

“Haha, you’re right. I need to stick around a bit longer so I can spoil Rio-chan with some pocket money.”  

“Yes, please do! I’ll take it!”  

…Wait, did a working adult just casually accept that?  

Before I could process that odd exchange, Rio abruptly changed the subject.  

“Anyway, we’ll get to the pocket money later. By the way, Grandpa Shuuji, are you thirsty right now?”  

Out of nowhere, Rio transitioned the conversation to the potion. That was… a rather aggressive pivot.

+++

# 216. Chill Drink

“Huh? Thirsty? …Uh, well, yeah, I’ve been here for a while, so I guess I am… thirsty… maybe…? Haha…” 

Souda-san awkwardly accepts the curveball from Aihara, a testament to his years of experience. It seems he’s well accustomed to Aihara’s sudden antics.  

However, Aihara is oblivious to his effort to adapt. She beams with a carefree smile, practically bouncing with excitement.  

“Whoa, really?! That’s perfect! I have the best drink, and I’ll give it to you, Grandpa Shuuji! Hey, Senpai, bring it out! You know, *that thing*!”  

“O-oh… sure…”  

Prompted by a grinning Aihara, I took a plastic bottle and some paper cups out of my bag.  

Incidentally, the potion was in the bottle. But here on Earth, with no magical essence, potions deteriorate more quickly. To combat this, I store them in my [Storage Space] and only pretend to retrieve them from my bag.  

“Oh? Matsunaga-san, do you normally carry things like this around?”  

Souda-san narrowed his already slender eyes, inspecting the bottle suspiciously.  

Well, who could blame him? It’s odd to have someone pushing drinks on you this insistently, especially since the bottle label (originally for cola) was removed. It makes it look even more dubious.  

But if he has concerns, I’d really appreciate it if he directed them at Aihara, not me. I didn’t expect her to be so pushy about this. When she confidently told me, “Leave everything to me! I’ve got this, it’s like my home turf!” I foolishly believed her.  

“Come on, Grandpa Shuuji, don’t sweat the small stuff! You said you’re thirsty, right? Go on, give it a try! It’ll blow your mind!”  

Please stop saying things like “it’ll blow your mind,” it makes this seem even more suspicious. But Aihara, blissfully unaware of my silent protests, eagerly poured the liquid into a paper cup and held it out to Souda-san.  

Reluctantly, he accepted the cup, though he didn’t drink it immediately. Instead, he looked at Aihara with a hesitant smile.  

“R-Rio-chan. So, what exactly is this drink? It looks like water, but…”  

“Huh? This? Oh, it’s, uh… yeah! It’s my latest obsession—a **chill drink**!”  

“Chill…?”  

“Yeah, chill! Don’t you know, Grandpa Shuuji? These days, drinks that make you feel all relaxed~~ calm~~ and gooey~~ are super popular!”  

“T-that wouldn’t happen to be something illegal, would it…?”  

“As if! Oh my gosh, Grandpa Shuuji, you’re hilarious! You crack me up!”  

Aihara laughed heartily, but I’m pretty sure Souda-san wasn’t joking.  

He let out a long sigh, then said,  

“Well… I suppose it doesn’t matter. I’m not long for this world anyway, so there’s no point worrying about it. And if it’s something Rio-chan is giving me, then…”  

With that, he tipped the paper cup back and downed the potion in one gulp—  

“_Gah, cough, hack! Cough, cough, hack!_”  

Only to start choking spectacularly.  

“Wait, Grandpa Shuuji, are you okay?! That’s what happens when you chug it all at once!” 

“_Cough… cough_… Yeah… maybe I overdid it a little—_cough!_”

“Don’t talk! You’re getting old, Grandpa Shuuji, so you’ve gotta take better care of your body! Come on, try breathing slowly. Alright, ready? _Hoo, hoo, haaa. Hoo, hoo, haaa. Hoo, hoo, haaa_.”  

With her brow furrowed in concern, Aihara gently rubbed his back, reciting Lamaze breathing techniques for some reason. I didn’t even have the energy to comment. But after a while, Souda-san’s condition seemed to stabilize.  

(Note: Lamaze breathing is a conscious breathing technique that focuses on slow, deep breaths.)

“……_Phew_, I’m feeling much better now. Thank you, Rio-chan. Sorry for troubling you.”  

“This is nothing; don’t even worry about it!”

Aihara smiled, looking quite pleased despite everything. It felt like she was enjoying this too much. But maybe it was just my imagination.  

As Souda-san took a moment to catch his breath, a female nurse walked toward us. She stopped in front of us and bowed politely.  

“Mr. Souda-san, I apologize for interrupting your conversation. But it’s time for your regular checkup. What would you like to do?”  

“Oh, today’s the day for that, is it? My apologies, I had completely forgotten. …Rio-chan, Matsunaga-san, I must excuse myself. I couldn’t quite grasp the taste of that drink, but I had a good time. It’s been a while since I’ve felt this way. I hope you’ll humor an old man again sometime. Goodbye for now.”  

With that, Souda-san grabbed his cane, which was propped against the bench, and attempted to stand. The nurse moved in quickly to assist him, showing her professionalism.  

“Hm…?”  

But just as he started to rise, he paused mid-motion. 

“Mr. Souda-san, is something the matter?”  

“No, it’s nothing.”  

Souda-san stood up straight and, to everyone’s surprise, began walking without even using his cane. Alarmed, the nurse hurried to his side.  

“Um, Mr. Souda-san, what about your legs…?”  

“Oh, they feel quite good today. Perhaps spending time with young folks did me some good.”  

With that, Souda-san left the courtyard, accompanied by the nurse.  

I watched him go, then turned to Aihara.  

“What do you make of that?”  

“Huh? What do you mean, ‘what do I make of that’…? Oh!”  

Aihara’s eyes widened, and she covered her mouth with both hands before exclaiming:  

“I forgot to ask him for pocket money…”  

She slumped forward in defeat.  

—After that, we continued to walk through the VIP ward, distributing free samples of the potion.  

In the end, though, Aihara’s absurd plan only worked on Souda-san. Her other elderly acquaintances politely declined, clearly uninterested.  

It made sense. These people seemed particularly health-conscious. And it’s no wonder they wouldn’t drink something suspicious. Honestly, we were lucky no one reported us.  

That said, I think my presence didn’t help. Having a stranger like me by her side probably heightened their caution.  

In that sense, it was remarkable that Souda-san drank it. But considering he seemed to have already accepted his mortality, it felt like he’d been half-indifferent to the risks.  

Still, the fact that he drank it might lead to the best possible outcome. At least, I couldn’t shake that feeling.  

As for Aihara, she seemed a bit down about the results. But when I treated her to some cheap cake at a family restaurant near the hospital under the guise of a “review session,” her mood immediately improved. What a simple person—though that worked out for me.  

◇◇◇

By evening, I parted ways with Aihara and headed home.  

I wondered how Colin, whom I had entrusted to Isezaki-san, was doing. With that thought, I made my way to the Isezaki residence.

+++

# 217. The Isezaki Residence and the Maid

“Uncle, thank you for your hard work. Please, come inside.”  

“Welcome back, Matsunaga-sama!”  

When I visited the Isezaki residence, I was greeted by Isezaki-san and Colin. While removing my shoes at the entrance, I spoke to Colin.  

“Colin-chan, how did you find Japan? You went shopping, right?”  

“Yes! I was taken to a building called a shopping mall! I even rode on an escalator and an elevator, and Lady Isezaki bought me many souvenirs. I, um… Lady Isezaki, thank you again! It was so much fun!”  

“Not at all, you’re very welcome.”  

Isezaki-san returned Colin’s enthusiastic bow of gratitude with a gentle smile. It seemed they went to the usual shopping mall. Thankfully, Colin handled the “escalator challenge” I was worried about without any trouble.  

“That’s great to hear. …By the way, did you buy any clothes for Colin-chan?”  

Colin was still wearing the maid outfit from the other world. I had heard from Isezaki-san that they planned to shop for casual clothes for her.  

“Well, we had Colin-chan try on several outfits, but—”  

“I greatly appreciated their generosity, but I declined because my usual uniform is the most practical for movement! Considering my duties as a bodyguard, I cannot compromise on this! Hah! Take this!”  

With that declaration, Colin threw a straight punch and followed it with a roundhouse kick aimed at thin air. Her enthusiasm was great, but the whooshing sound of her attacks was unsettling for someone her size.  

“I… I see. Well, I guess this maid outfit might not stand out too much here on Earth?”  

“Yes! It seems to be mistaken for something called cosplay, a type of costume.”  

“Since Colin-chan wears it so naturally, it didn’t attract as much attention as I thought it would.”  

“Ah, I see now.”  

Now that they mentioned it, if you saw a child in a maid outfit, you might find it charming rather than think she was an actual maid. Perhaps it’s just barely acceptable.  

As we continued talking, I noticed something. Colin’s Japanese was starting to sound more like her usual speech from the other world. It seemed she had quickly picked up on the peculiarity of Aihara’s phrasing and adjusted accordingly. As expected of a child prodigy—her adaptability was astounding.  

We eventually reached the guest room, and Colin called out toward the sliding doors.  

“Madam, I’ve brought Matsunaga-sama!”  

“Alright, let him in.”  

…Ah, so it’s “Madam” after all. I suppose the landlady instructed her to call her that. Feeling the depth of the challenges in learning Japanese, I stepped into the guest room.  

◇◇◇

The TV in the guest room was left on, playing an anime about a futuristic cat-shaped robot. Apparently, Colin had been watching it while waiting for me. She glanced back at the screen with a longing expression before stepping out with Isezaki-san to prepare tea.  

Meanwhile, I found myself sitting across the table from Isezaki Haruna, the owner of this house and my landlady. She was wearing her usual black T-shirt, maintaining her signature rock-and-funky style.  

She took a sip from her teacup, then raised an intrigued eyebrow at me.  

“Hey, Matsunaga-kun. I heard from Seina that you delivered potions to the hospital. How did the business go?”  

“Well… they were pretty cautious, so almost no one accepted them. Only one person tried a potion.”  

“Haha, I see. So even young lady Rio couldn’t break through. Still, considering it’s a place full of stubborn old men and women, having even one person drink it is a win.”  

“That’s true. But I think if I hadn’t gone along, more people might have tried it. I feel like I messed up there.”  

“…Oh? For someone who says that, you don’t seem too down about it.”  

“Eh? Do I?”  

“Yes. Even I can tell that much. So, who was the kind soul who drank it?”  

“Souda Shuuji-san. He used to work for Juuzou-san’s company. Do you know him?”  

“Ah, Souda? Of course, I know him. I see… you’ve landed yourself quite a catch there.”  

“Really? If you say so, Landlady, I feel a bit more reassured.” 

“Well, you never know how things will play out, depending on the circumstances. But with you, Matsunaga-kun, I’m sure you’ll manage—”  

“Excuse me!”  

Suddenly, a voice interrupted us. Turning to look, I saw Colin trembling slightly as she carried a tray of tea. While Isezaki-san brought a plate of tea snacks.  

“Hey, girls. Why don’t you sit down, too?”  

“Yes, Madam!”  “Yes, Grandmother.”  

Colin plopped down next to me, while Isezaki-san sat on the opposite side. Ah, right. I needed to thank them first.  

“Landlady, it seems Colin-chan was in your care today… Thank you very much.”  

I bowed my head, and the landlady smirked in amusement.  

“No need for thanks. All I did was chat with her a bit. It felt like spending time with a great-grandchild—very enjoyable. …Well, if it were my real great-grandchild, they’d probably be even cuter. I wonder when that’ll happen.”  

“Haha, I wouldn’t worry about it. Isezaki-san is quite popular, so I’m sure marriage and great-grandchildren will come sooner than you think.”  

“Hmph. That would be nice… wouldn’t it, Seina?”  

“Yes, Grandmother… Heh.”  

For some reason, Isezaki-san replied with a frosty tone. Oh no, talking about marriage and grandchildren to a young woman was probably crossing the line. This might have been a misstep on my part.  

Fortunately, the landlady quickly shifted the conversation.  

“—Well, putting that aside, Colin’s staying in Japan for a while, right? You said she’s here as a bodyguard. What’s your plan for that?”  

“Uh, well… For now, it looks like she’ll accompany me whenever I go out. Not that I think I need it.”  

“It’s a generous offer from Princess Levia. Don’t be ungrateful—accept it graciously. You’ve got a bit of a laid-back and careless side, Matsunaga-kun. She might come in handy.”  

“Haha, maybe so…”  

“But what about Colin’s sleeping arrangements? She insists she has to stay at your house to properly guard you.”  

“Yeah, that’s the problem.”  

The plan, suggested by Isezaki-san, was for Colin to stay at the Isezaki residence. However, convincing her had proven difficult.  

“Nighttime is prime time for attacks! I cannot allow myself to be separated from the person I’m guarding during sleep!”  

That was her reasoning. Colin continued,  

“Moreover, Lady Levia has instructed me to ensure Lady Isezaki’s safety as well. Therefore, I propose that Lady Isezaki also stays at Matsunaga-sama’s residence!”  

“That’s an excellent idea, Colin-chan!”  

Even Isezaki-san leaned forward, agreeing enthusiastically with Colin’s suggestion. No, no, please spare me from this.  

“A young woman staying in my room in Japan. Even if it’s fine in another world, it is absolutely out of the question. Besides, that tiny room can’t fit three people.”  

“Haha, you’ve got some nerve saying that in front of the landlady.”  

“I-I’m sorry!”  

That was strike two for the day. 

“Still, Matsunaga-kun, Colin seems pretty set on this.”  

“Ugh… In that case, I’ll sleep on the floor, and Colin-chan can take the bed—”  

“I’m fine with the floor! I can even sleep standing if needed, so no worries!”  

“That would just make me feel worse…”  

I had to figure out a way to convince Colin. There had to be some way for her to guard me without being in the same room.  

As I fell silent, the guest room grew quiet. The only sound was the faint audio from the TV playing the futuristic cat-shaped robot anime.  

“Ah, I’ve got it!”  

If it worked, this idea could solve everything. I decided to try out a new spatial-time magic immediately.

+++

# 218. The Gate That’s Not Just Anywhere

“Um… there’s something I’d like to try.”

“Oh? I don’t know what it is, but go ahead and give it a shot.”

With their approval, I stood up and scanned the area. I was searching for a suitable wall. My eyes landed on the sliding fusuma doors in the guest room we had just passed through. Perfect. The rectangular shape of the fusuma seemed ideal for what I had in mind.  

(Note:

![](https://i0.wp.com/dragonholic.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/08/fusuma.jpg?resize=275%2C183&ssl=1)

Fusuma doors

)

I placed my palm against the fusuma, focusing my mind.  

What I was envisioning was not just any door, but… a gate. Yes, a gate rather than a door. Unlike a door, a gate didn’t necessarily need to have a physical barrier.  

Concentrating deeply, I pictured the gate in my mind. Gradually, the space in front of me warped to match the shape of the fusuma. And a jet-black void emerged, as though ink had spilled across it.  

“…….!”  

I heard gasps from the three people observing behind me. However, this wasn’t much different from the usual void I summoned. It wasn’t complete yet.  

I refined the image of the gate in my mind. What exactly was a gate? It wasn’t merely an entry or exit. It was something that defined boundaries, separating the inside from the outside. It wasn’t strange to imagine an entirely different world unfolding on the other side of the gate.  

I willed myself to believe in the existence of a place beyond this black void—a place that shouldn’t exist, yet was there. And then—  

Ripples began to spread across the darkness. The undulating ripples gradually erased the blackness. And from the center of the ripples, a familiar scene started to appear.  

“This is… Uncle’s room!?”  

Indeed, as Isezaki-san said. The scene before us was my room in the Haruna apartment, where I had lived since my university days.  

“Yeah, that’s right. Let’s call this… hmm, the [Void Gate]. I’ll test it out now.”  

“Ah, Uncle—!”  

Ignoring her startled shout, I stepped through the [Void Gate] into the other side—my room—without any discomfort.  

The familiar feel of the cheap carpet under my socked feet, surrounded by the inexpensive furniture and bed, confirmed that this was unmistakably my room.  

Turning around, I could see through the [Void Gate] into the guest room. The three onlookers were staring at me from the other side. The spaces were still connected.  

Alright, it seemed my new spatial magic had worked.  

“What do you think? I’ve linked my room to the guest room over there—”  

“Uncle, let me check too!”  

Isezaki-san exclaimed as she darted through the [Void Gate] into my room. The moment she entered, she closed her eyes and took a deep breath.  

“_Suuu-haaa… suuu-haaa… suuu-haaa…_” 

“Uh, Isezaki-san? What are you doing?”  

“_Suuu-haa_—! Ah! S-sorry! Um, well…! The air in Uncle’s room was so refreshing, I couldn’t help but take a deep breath!”  

Wait, what? My room? Refreshing air? I mean, I guess it’s better than being told it smells like an old man’s room, but still.  

“Excuse me.”  

“Pardon us!”  

Before I could find the words to respond, the landlady and Colin entered my room as well. The landlady surveyed the space, nodding approvingly.  

“Whew, it’s been a while since I’ve seen this place. Looks like you’ve kept it in good shape.”

“Of course. You told me from the start that you wouldn’t rent to anyone who didn’t take good care of the room.”  

The rent was affordable even for a student, and it hadn’t increased since then. To keep such a deal, I had been meticulous about maintaining the place.  

“Good memory, Matsunaga-kun. Well done.”  

“Matsunaga-sama! With this… it’s perfectly… fine… isn’t it!”  

I turned toward Colin, who was now leaping back and forth through the [Void Gate]. She frantically crossed between my room and the guest room at an incredible speed. She moved so fast that she started to look like a blur, almost as though she was duplicating herself.  

I nodded, satisfied with the results. 

“Exactly. You can even hear sounds from the other side. So, even if something strange happens while you’re staying at Isezaki-san’s estate, you can immediately return to my room, right?” 

“Yes, absolutely!”

“Heh, that’s an impressive bit of magic. By the way, with this [Void Gate], could you go to London or LA?”  

“No, I can’t. Or rather, it only works for places I’ve been to before…”  

That aspect of it is no different from [Dimensional Teleport]. I can’t connect the [Void Gate] to any place I haven’t visited. Forget London or Los Angeles—I’ve never even been abroad.  

“I see, so it’s not an ‘anywhere-you-want’ kind of thing. I thought it might be like *that* thing,” 

The landlady teased, gesturing toward the anime playing in the guest room.  

Please, don’t set such high expectations for a regular guy like me.  

“But! I’ve never seen or heard of magic like this before. As expected of you, Uncle!”  

“Haha, thanks.”  

As I casually responded to Isezaki-san’s typical over-the-top praise, I felt relieved that the issue of Colin’s lodging seemed to be resolved.  

◇◇◇

Later, after consulting with the Isezaki family, we decided to keep a permanent [Void Gate] between my home and the Isezaki estate while Colin stayed there.  

For the record, as long as I supply it with magic, the [Void Gate] can remain active indefinitely. In essence, my home temporarily became an annex of the Isezaki estate.  

Of course, I sought renewed permission from both the landlady and Isezaki-san. And honestly, I was surprised they allowed it. I mean, isn’t it weird? Connecting a random guy’s house to theirs, even if he’s not family?  

Determined to live up to their trust, I resolved to live even more respectfully and responsibly than before.  

For starters, I decided not to use the [Void Gate] for convenience. If I needed to visit the Isezaki residence, I’d go through the front door like a normal guest. Manners matter, after all.  

However, the [Void Gate] did create one small but significant problem: I no longer had any privacy.  

Since the guest room where Colin was staying and my room were now connected, my private space was effectively exposed. Having a live-in guard is no joke. If I desperately needed alone time, I’d have to lock myself in the bathroom or something.  

With this new issue on my mind, I nonetheless took my first solid step forward toward helping Lady Levia and furthering my potion sales endeavors.

+++

# 219. A Free Day

In the depths of sleep… a faint voice echoed from afar.  

I couldn’t quite make out what was being said, but the sound was soothing somehow. Letting the murmur wash over me, I sank deeper into my slumber—  

_(—Lady Isezaki, what brings you here at such a late hour? Is there an emergency?)_  

_(Eek! C-Colin dear, you’re awake?)_  

_(I’m on guard duty, so I wake up quickly. Ahem! So, what business do you have?)_  

_(Um, well, it’s not exactly business… I just thought I’d, um, check on Uncle while he’s sleeping—no, no, I mean, wish him a good night…)_  

_(Hmm? But you already said good night earlier, didn’t you? Matsunaga-sama has been asleep for quite a while now.)_  

_(Oh, r-right! Now that you mention it… I guess I got confused. Maybe I’m still a little groggy.)_  

_(I understand. When I was little, I once threw a knife at a noise in my sleepwalking state. It was only to find it was my sister checking on me. She was furious! I don’t do that anymore, though.)_  

_(O-oh, I see… Oh, I just had a great idea! If Uncle is asleep, wouldn’t it be easier for you to guard him if I slept in the same bed? It’s brilliant! I’ll go right now—)_  

_(Hold on!)_  

_(Wah, Colin dear, when did you get in front of me?)_  

_(Please rest comfortably in your own room, Lady Isezaki. If guarding you becomes a burden on the target, I would be failing as a protector. Now, please return. Shoo, shoo!)_  

_(O-okay, okay, stop pushing! Well then, Colin dear, do your best with your duties. Good night…)_  

_(Good night!)_  

_(…Muu,_*_pout_*_…)_  

◇◇◇  

The next day. Perhaps thanks to my familiar bed, I had the best sleep I’d had in a while. I vaguely recall waking up to a noise once during the night, but it didn’t bother me.  

Today, Isezaki-san was at the academy, and Aihara was at work.  

As for me, I wanted to push forward with the potion sales. But it seemed unlikely anyone would try the potions at the VIP ward just a day after our first attempt. I decided it would be better to wait for Souda-san’s regular check-up results before making a move.  

Thus, today ended up being a rare free day for me.  

It’s a bit sad to call it rare when I’m unemployed, but I couldn’t just laze around at home watching TV or reading manga. Especially while the Isezaki estate was connected to the [Void Gate]—I had to maintain a respectable lifestyle in case someone like Isezaki-san or the landlady decided to drop by.  

So, I resolved to spend today as a model unemployed individual and head outside. But given my lack of outdoor hobbies, my activities were pretty limited: buying groceries and household goods, or visiting the 100-yen shops to stock up on items for sale in the other world.  

Since I already had enough food and supplies, I decided today’s outing would focus on 100-yen shop hopping. For someone like me, trying to be frugal, it was a perfect plan.  

However, there was a minor problem. Lately, I felt like some of the staff at certain 100-yen shops were starting to recognize me. It might just be my imagination, but…  

I didn’t mind if they found me amusing, but I didn’t want to be mistaken for a reseller. I mean, I am reselling the stuff, but it’s in another world. So they should cut me some slack!  

To avoid suspicion, I decided to venture out to a 100-yen shop I’d never visited before, somewhere farther away. Not only would it expand my shopping range, but it would also broaden the reach of my [Dimensional Teleport] ability—a win-win!
