For transportation, I planned to use a car. My rough plan was to drive around 100-yen shops and even cross into the neighboring prefecture.  

Of course, I’m a paper driver and don’t own a car. So I rented one. I opted for a plan that allowed me to return the car to a different rental station, making it easy to teleport back home after my long trip.  

And so, I smoothly rented a car at the rental agency.  

All that was left was to hop in and drive off—when suddenly, a small incident made me break into a cold sweat.  

At the car rental agency, the woman showing us the car smiled warmly and spoke to Colin.  

“Fufu, are you going on a drive with your dad today?”  

“This man is not my dad! Matsunaga-sama is my guardee!”  

“Wha…?”  

The woman’s expression stiffened. I hadn’t expected anyone to talk to Colin, so I hadn’t prepared for this scenario at all.  

“S-sorry! Uh, this girl is my relative, and she’s really into role-playing these days…”  

I hurriedly tried to cover it up. Colin, however, quickly followed up.  

“…! Yes, that’s it! Sorry for surprising you, miss!”  

“O-oh, I see… It looks good on you and is super cute.”  

“Thank you!”  

Colin flashed a bright smile, and the woman returned a slightly awkward grin. Crisis averted. Colin’s ability to think on her feet was truly impressive—what a genius.  

I had been pretty relaxed since Isezaki-san once mentioned that being with Colin didn’t draw much attention. But now that I thought about it, a regular guy in his thirties walking around with a foreign-looking little girl in a maid outfit was bound to attract stares.  

Sure, Colin might seem less conspicuous when standing next to someone like Isezaki-san, who naturally drew attention. But with me? The contrast was way too glaring.  

Come to think of it, the woman might have suspected something like a kidnapping and approached us out of concern. I’ll need to have a discussion with Colin later about coming up with a proper backstory.  

Anyway, with the awkward encounter resolved, I placed Colin in the passenger seat and pressed the accelerator.

+++

# 220. Colin's First Shopping Trip

Since I was a paper driver, I was a bit anxious. But no matter who presses the accelerator, the car will start moving. Despite my clumsy driving, the scenery outside the window gradually began to flow by.

“Matsunaga-sama! The car is moving! It’s much faster than a carriage!!”

“Y-Yeah, that’s right. By the way, Colin-chan, in Japan, someone like me—just an ordinary guy—wouldn’t have a bodyguard. So, maybe we should reconsider that setup.”

“Is that so? When I asked Lady Isezaki, she said, ‘For someone as amazing as Uncle, it wouldn’t be strange for him to have a bodyguard…'” 

“Yeah, that’s not quite right.”

It seemed that behind Colin’s statement, Isezaki-san had been working behind the scenes. She still seems to be overly flattering me, but if I think of it as a sign of trust. It’s kind of endearing… or at least, I think it might be.

In any case, I discussed it with Colin and ended up developing the idea I had casually mentioned earlier about a relative’s child. It turned into a story where my sister (who doesn’t exist) has a daughter with a foreign husband.

She’s a cute, highly capable child prodigy. And I think this setup makes more sense than saying she’s the child of an average person like me. I’ll make sure to inform Isezaki-san and Aihara about this later.

—

After driving for a while, we arrived at our first destination. It was a large shopping mall located at the border of the prefecture. I heard that there was a 100-yen shop among the mall’s tenants. This was my first time actually visiting.

Whether it was out of curiosity or because of her role as my bodyguard, Colin looked around, her eyes darting everywhere. So I accompanied her into the 100-yen shop.

I began by picking up some standard items: lighters, pens, LED lights, and plenty of batteries. These were things I’d been told by the handsome merchant, Ryas from the Reymar Trading Company, that were in high demand and seriously lacking in stock. Whenever I saw them, I made sure to buy them.

That said, just buying the usual products is boring. Since I was there to explore new items for the shop, I figured I might as well look for something that could become a hit—something new and interesting.

I wandered around the store for a bit. But in the end, I didn’t find anything that really caught my eye.

Well, of course. If a beginner like me could suddenly become a skilled buyer, it wouldn’t be much of a challenge. But on the bright side, I came up with a good idea.

—If I want to know what people from another world want, I can just ask people from that world. So, I decided to ask Colin.

“Um… Colin-chan, are there any items in this store that might be rare or unique in the other world?”

“Hmm, if that’s the case—it’s over there!”

Apparently, she already had something in mind. Colin walked off, so I followed her. She stopped in front of a shelf, and there it was—

“Eh? A calendar?”

“A calendar…? Ah, I see! This character represents the calendar, doesn’t it?”

“That’s right. Don’t people in the other world have calendars like this?”

“They do, but nothing as fancy as this. But the reason I thought it was rare wasn’t just because of that. Look here!”

She pointed to the usual section of the calendar with pictures of landscapes, dogs, and cats printed on it.

“I’ve never seen pictures like these—more delicate and realistic than paintings!”

“Ah, I see.”

I could definitely see this item selling well. The Reymar Trading Company targets the wealthy. And rich people often want rare paintings and will pay a large sum for them… or maybe that’s just a prejudice on my part.

Now that I think about it, when I sold canned tuna at the Reymar Trading Company, the buyers were more interested in the photo printed on the can than the actual contents.

Also, since the calendar had decent photos for each of the six months, all priced at 100 yen, it seemed like a bargain. 

I could just cut out the photo part of the calendar and have Ryas frame them in a nice frame to add some luxury. This could definitely be worth a try.

“Colin-chan, you’re amazing. I’m going to go with your idea.”

“Did I do a good job?”

“Yeah, yeah, great job!”

“Yay!”

Colin bounced up and down, looking very pleased. She seemed especially happy to be praised for something other than her bodyguard duties. She wore a very satisfied expression.

“…….You know, as a reward for your good work, Colin-chan. How about I buy you something from this store? Anything you want, just tell me.”

“Eh, but…”

Colin hesitated, her eyes downcast. She looked like she was trying to hold back. She seemed reluctant, but she kept glancing at a shelf in the distance. It looked like she really wanted something but was too shy to ask.

“Come on, kids don’t need to hold back. If you want something, just tell me.”

“…….Is it really alright?”

“Of course.”

Sighing in resignation at my insistence, Colin lowered her head politely.

“Thank you very much for your kindness! Well then, I’ll go ahead and say what I want—”

She headed straight for the kitchen section, where various dishes and kitchen gadgets were displayed in a crowded space. Given that Colin, a maid, wasn’t particularly good at housework, this was an unexpected choice.

Maybe she planned to practice cooking in Japan. If that was the case, I thought it was a great attitude to have. If that’s the case, I’d buy whatever she needed, no problem.

“This one! I want as many as possible!”

With sparkling eyes, Colin pointed eagerly at something. Wait, what!?

There, lined up on the shelf, were small knives—petty knives.

“Eh… I see… What kind of dishes do you plan to use them for?”

I already had a bad feeling, but I asked anyway.

“No, I thought they’d be perfect for throwing! They’re a bit too light to deal a fatal blow, but they seem great for intimidation and deterrence! As soon as I saw them, I knew they were just right for that! Right now, there are only these two.”

Ah, I knew it… I stiffened as Colin, without paying any attention to my troubled expression, lifted the long skirt of her maid outfit up to her thighs. There, like some spy, two knives were strapped to her leg with a band.

The blades of the knives had fine scratches, giving them a used look. And they had a certain quality about them that spoke to craftsmanship. The handles, however, seemed poorly maintained. It had something red and black staining them that sent a chill down my spine.

Then I realized I was staring at the thighs of a little girl, which made me feel socially cold too.

That aside, a man’s word is his bond. I took all the petty knives off the shelf, grabbing about ten of them, and tossed them into the shopping basket.

“Wow! Thank you so much!”

Colin’s cheerful voice caused the other customers nearby to turn around, and everyone couldn’t help but smile at her beaming face. However, no one would ever guess the reason for her smile was that she had just been given throwing knives. As I thought about this, I could only smile wryly to myself.

+++

# 221. Colin's First Shopping Trip: Afterward

While pretending not to notice the store clerk’s strained expression at the sheer volume of knives in our shopping basket, Colin and I finished paying and left the 100-yen shop.  

This wasn’t the only 100-yen shop we planned to visit today. We had to move briskly to hit them all.  

—

After that, Colin and I hopped from one 100-yen shop to another as if we were on a stamp rally. And before we knew it, the sun had completely set.  

The shopping spree was largely uneventful—there were no significant troubles, and Colin wasn’t approached by anyone. Which meant the elaborate backstory I had prepared for her went unused. A bit of a shame, honestly.  

The one thing that stood out was how Colin seemed eager to drive after watching me closely. In the beginning, her mimicking my steering motions was just cute. But as she got more comfortable, she started commenting when I missed a turn during a right-hand maneuver or advising, “You should get into the right lane now,” while watching the GPS. She had become the slightly annoying type of passenger. Sorry, I’m just a paper driver…  

That aside, this drive seemed to have been an exhilarating experience for Colin. The sparkle in her eyes as she enjoyed herself left quite an impression.  

Though the trip was part of my frugal budgeting efforts, I’m glad Colin had fun too.  

Afterward, I returned the rental car at an office across the prefectural border and used **[Dimensional Teleport]** to get back home.  

—

Next on the agenda was dropping Colin off at the Isezaki residence, setting up the **[Void Gate]** in the guest room, and wrapping up the day’s tasks.  

That’s how I ended up visiting the Isezaki residence. At the entrance, Isezaki-san greeted us with a warm smile.  

“Uncle, Colin-chan, you went out today, didn’t you? Thank you for your hard work.”  

“Yep, we did. And here’s a little souvenir for you—these are for you and the landlady to enjoy.”  

I handed her some specialty buns I’d picked up at a roadside station along the way.  

“Oh my, thank you so much… Wait, you went quite far today, didn’t you?”  

Noticing the label on the buns, Isezaki-san blinked in surprise.  

“Yeah, I thought I’d check out some new 100-yen shops. Ended up going to the neighboring prefecture for the first time in a while.”  

“I got to ride in a car today! _Vroom, vroom! Screeeech!”_ 

Colin enthusiastically mimicked driving, complete with sound effects. While it was endearing, I wish she hadn’t recreated the sudden brake and jolt that occurred at one point.  

Isezaki-san tilted her head at Colin’s actions.  

“A car? But Uncle, you don’t own one, do you?”  

“True, but this time I rented one. Colin and I went on a little trip to some 100-yen shops outside the prefecture. It was my first time driving in ages, but we managed.”  

“W-Wait a moment! U-Uncle… You… went on a drive… with Colin today?”  

“Uh, yeah, I guess you could call it that?”  

“I… I haven’t even…”  

“Um, is something wrong, Isezaki-san?”  

Noticing her leaning against the wall, muttering something, I asked if she was okay. She lightly shook her head and gave me a faint, wistful smile.  

“No, it’s nothing. More importantly, Colin-chan, how was your drive with Uncle? Where did you go?”  

With a bright smile, Isezaki-san shifted her focus to Colin.  

“Well… for lunch, we went to a kaiten sushi place. The plates spinning around were so fun! And I tried copying Matsunaga-sama by putting wasabi on my sushi. But it was so spicy I cried! It’s amazing how he can eat it like it’s delicious!”  

“I… see. Sounds like you had fun. What else?”  

“I saw the ocean from the car! I’d never seen the ocean before, and it was so big—so incredibly big!”  

“Th-that’s… nice…”  

“Then, the sunset was so beautiful that Matsunaga-sama took a picture of it as a keepsake! Oh, Matsunaga-sama, could you show me the photo from back then?” 

“Sure, here you go.”  

I operated my smartphone and showed Colin the screen.  

The picture was just an amateur snapshot taken on a road overlooking the ocean, with Colin in the foreground against the sunset. An old man holding a fishing rod was awkwardly in the frame too.  

But seeing it, Colin’s face lit up with joy.  

“Wow, it’s really so beautiful! Thank you for taking this, Matsunaga-sama!”  

“Really? If you like it that much, I’ll print it out for you next time. Feel free to take it home.”  

“Yay! I’m so happy! Oh, and please print the one we took together too!”  

“Ah, that one? If you don’t mind having me in it, of course—”  

**_—Thud!_**  

Suddenly, there was a loud noise of something hitting the floor. Turning to look, I saw Isezaki-san collapsed to her knees.  

“Isezaki-san!? What’s wrong? Are you okay!?”  

Was it anemia? Isezaki-san lowered her head, trembling.  

“Ugh… uuuugh…”  

“Huh?”  

When she raised her face, her brows were furrowed tightly. And in a trembling voice, she spoke.  

“—I’m jealous…!”  

“What?”  

“Uncle, I wanted… I wanted to go on a drive too! I wanted to have pictures taken too!”  

“Eh? No, no, it was just a trip to pick up supplies from some 100-yen shops. The photos weren’t even of any scenic spots or anything…”  

But Isezaki-san wasn’t listening. She clenched her fists and looked at me with determined eyes.

“Uncle!”  

“Y-Yes!?”  

“Next time, please, please take me on a drive too!”  

“Uh, well…”  

“I don’t care where! Even to a 100-yen shop, the local supermarket, or a convenience store! I just want to go on a drive with you, that’s all!”  

While I was flustered by her sudden request, Colin nodded knowingly for some reason.  

“Yes, yes, I understand! Matsunaga-sama’s driving is so entertaining! Trusting yourself to such an unstable vehicle that doesn’t behave the way you want is thrilling and exciting!”  

It was probably her honest opinion, but why did it sound like a diss?  

Anyway—  

I looked again at Isezaki-san’s face. She was utterly serious; it didn’t seem like she was joking.  

Well, maybe she felt a little left out after hearing Colin talk so enthusiastically about the trip. That wasn’t hard to understand.  

If that’s the case, I should take her feelings into account. 

“Alright. Then next time I go shopping, would you like to come too, Isezaki-san?”  

It was just a simple errand run, nothing fancy. Colin had enjoyed it because she was from another world, after all.  

But to my surprise, Isezaki-san’s face lit up with a radiant smile. And she grabbed my hand tightly.  

“Really!? I’ll definitely come! Promise me! Promise! Promise!”  

“Haha… Just remember, I’m not the best driver.”  

“I don’t care about that. Hehe, I’m already looking forward to it!”  

She hopped lightly, unusually excited.  

Honestly, riding in my car is less comfortable and safe than having her usual chauffeur take her in a luxury car. But if this makes her happy, then I guess it’s fine.  

Watching Isezaki-san’s childlike excitement, I let out a relieved sigh. I was glad I managed to settle things for now.

+++

# 222. Material Delivery

The day after our shopping trip to the hundred-yen store. I began a new job assigned by Lady Levia: transporting supplies to the magic stone mine.  

In the morning, I teleported with my guard, Colin, using [Dimensional Teleport] to Lady Levia’s castle. There, I met Holly, who was already waiting for me. According to her, the materials for this trip had been gathered into one location. It left me only the task of collecting them. Lady Levia was busy with various matters and wasn’t present.  

After finishing our discussion, Holly, for the first time, turned her gaze toward Colin instead of focusing solely on me.  

“Colin, is the guarding going well?”  

“So far, I haven’t encountered anyone harboring ill intentions toward Matsunaga-sama or Lady Isezaki! The other world is truly peaceful, without any monsters. It’s so calm that I’m worried my skills might dull!”  

“I see. It really is a peaceful world, then.”  

“Yes! It’s peaceful, and so much fun! Yesterday, Matsunaga-sama took me to all sorts of places! Ehehe!”  

Colin’s carefree smile beamed as she spoke informally, while Holly averted her eyes apologetically.  

“Matsunaga-sama, I’m sorry if Colin has been a bother—”  

“No, no, she just accompanies me wherever I go. It’s no trouble at all.”  

“I understand. But Colin, even in the calmest worlds, unexpected dangers can always lurk. A guard’s duty is to prevent such risks before they happen. Stay vigilant in your mission.”  

“Yes, ma’am!”  

“Keep your replies concise.”  

“Yes!”  

“Good. Now then, Matsunaga-sama. Please allow me to guide you.”  

With the conversation over, Holly turned to me with a composed expression. She remained the same cool-headed maid as always. However, when Colin said it had been “fun”, I noticed a slight softening at the corners of her mouth.  

Though Holly seemed stern, she likely cared deeply for her younger sister—especially since Colin was stationed in a world so different from her own.  

As these thoughts crossed my mind, I followed Holly to a nearby plaza. It was the same place where materials for the fort at the magic stone mine had been stored before.  

“This is the location, Matsunaga-sama. Please take care of it.”  

Holly bowed gracefully. Behind her stood a towering pile of materials: wood, stone, and large wooden crates filled with who-knows-what.  

These supplies had been painstakingly acquired by Lady Levia over the past few days, sparing no expense. And this was only the beginning—Lady Levia was actively securing more materials for the next shipment. Not only that, but she had also arranged for personnel to be dispatched through the adventurers’ guild.  

It was clear from the hustle of people and materials that the development of the magic stone mine was progressing at a rapid pace. Not wanting to fall behind, I decided to start immediately.  

I approached the mountain of supplies and began storing them into my [Storage Space] one after another.  

Even though I had done this numerous times before, there was something oddly satisfying about making the materials disappear one by one. It was like clearing blocks in a puzzle game. It was strangely addictive. I felt like I could do this kind of work for hours on end.  

In just a few minutes, the once-massive pile of supplies vanished without a trace. It left the open space as it was before.  

Watching quietly, Holly let out a small breath of amazement, her eyes narrowing slightly.  

“No matter how many times I witness it, your ability never ceases to amaze me. Thank you for your dedication to Lady Levia.”  

“Haha, feel free to use it whenever you need. I’ll head out now. I just need to meet with Captain Beard again, right?”  

“Captain…? Oh, you mean Commander Higuner. Yes, please report to him.”  

At some point, he had been promoted from captain to commander. I wasn’t entirely sure how that happened, but it was probably a well-earned advancement.  

“Got it. I’ll be off, then.”  

“Please wait! Colin should accompany you—”  

“Wait, Matsunaga-sama!”  

“It’s fine. I’ll be quick. You two enjoy some sisterly time at the castle.”  

Thinking it would be nice to let the sisters spend some time together, I teleported using [Dimensional Teleport] without waiting for Colin.  

(For the record, Colin’s incredible reflexes almost caught me with a tackle. That’s something worth noting.)  

◇◇◇  

“Hey! Move that lumber further inside!”  

“This way’s blocked! Clear the path!”  

“Two people can’t carry that! Somebody lend a hand!”  

“The ground over there is muddy! Watch your step!”  

It had been about a week since my last visit to the magic stone mine.  

This place was as lively as ever with the bustling activity of workers. And even from near the forward base where I had teleported, the lively noise carried clearly to my ears.  

I felt like wandering around a bit, but that wasn’t an option. After all, *that person* might show up if I dawdled.  

With that thought in mind, I headed quickly toward the forward base and met with Captain Beard, now promoted to Commander Beard.  

“Ah, Matsunaga-sama! We’ve been expecting you! I hear you’ve brought supplies from Grandain again!”  

Commander Beard approached cheerfully, his hands almost rubbing together in enthusiasm.  

“Yes, that’s correct. Now, could you please lead me to the warehouse right away?”  

“Of course! …However, since you seemed to leave in a hurry last time, why not take your time this time? I can assign a guide to show you around if you’d like to explore the area.”  

He maintained his cheerful smile as he leaned in with subtle pressure. He probably meant no harm, but his eagerness was a bit overwhelming.  

“N-no, I appreciate the offer, but I’ll pass this time. If I linger too long, ***she*** might show up. And that would be a hassle…”  

“*She*? Are you referring to Maristel-dono?”  

I nodded silently. Exactly—if I took my time, Maristel would come.  

I glanced nervously at the door behind me, half-expecting it to open at any moment, while mentally bracing for Maristel’s sudden appearance. But Commander Beard burst into laughter at my reaction.  

“Wahahahaha! What are you saying, Matsunaga-sama? Surely, you gave her a stern talking-to, didn’t you? Ever since your last visit, Maristel-dono has been remarkably well-behaved! She hasn’t caused any trouble these past few days!”  

Ah, I see. Commander Beard’s attitude toward me had been softening with each meeting. Apparently he thought I had *disciplined* Maristel. But still…  

“Well, I did tell her to try not to bother others too much. But she’s not the type to listen so easily. Maybe she’s just caught a cold or something?”  

“Wahaha! Maristel-dono with a cold? What a funny joke! …But, of course, we shouldn’t keep you too long. Let me take you to the warehouse right away! This way, please!”  

Although he didn’t take my comment seriously, he at least understood I was in a hurry. For all his cheerfulness, Commander Beard must be quite competent to command such a volatile frontline area.  

With Commander Beard leading the way, I headed to the warehouse, where I unloaded the supplies I had stored in my [Storage Space]. Commander Beard licked his lips at the sight of the massive pile of materials. With that, I had successfully completed the first supply delivery without incident.  

—Incidentally, I later found out that Maristel *really had* caught a cold. If I’d known, I might have paid her a visit… or maybe not. Hard to say.  

◇◇◇  

After that, I returned to my castle and reunited with Holly and her sister. Holly seemed softer than before. I made arrangements for the next transport, and then I returned to Japan.  

I spent a few hours at home before lunchtime. While Colin and I were slurping the cup noodles she had requested, a notification from LANE popped up on my phone.  

The sender was Mr. Jounai Juuzou. According to the message, Mr. Shouda wanted to meet me.  

There was only one reason why I’d be summoned—it must be that the results of Mr. Shouda’s routine medical check-up was in.  

After arranging the meeting with Mr. Juuzou, I decided to head to the hospital with Colin.

+++

# 223. Business Negotiation

Colin and I used [Dimensional Teleport] to arrive at Mr. Juuzou’s hospital room.

“Oh, you’re here. Good to see you,” 

Mr. Juuzou greeted us warmly as we appeared before him. He really had grown accustomed to this. After a brief exchange of greetings, his curious gaze fell on Colin.

“Hmm, so this is… the one?”

“Yes, she’s accompanying me as a bodyguard from another world—”

“I’m Colin! Nice to meet you!” 

“Oh, uh, yes. Nice to meet you too. Hmm… I’ve heard about you, but still, it’s hard to imagine such a small child being capable of serving as a bodyguard— No, wait. Forgive me. I’ve recently learned that applying my own logic to another world is… unwise.”

Scratching his cheek awkwardly, Mr. Juuzou seemed to recall a recent incident where his skepticism about the other world had angered Isezaki-san.

“She’s defeated one villain after another over there. Honestly, she’s far stronger than most adults.”

“Is that so? As small as she is… appearances can be deceiving.”

“Hehe.”

“Indeed, indeed,” 

Mr. Juuzou muttered, his expression softening as he looked at Colin. It was almost as if she were his grandchild. Of course, she hadn’t just defeated villains—she’d outright killed them—but I figured that part was better left unsaid to Mr. Juuzou.

“…So, then. Matsunaga, you’re planning to pitch that medicine to Shouda, aren’t you? I’ve known him for a long time, and I understand how to handle him. If you want, I could sit in with you.”

“Thank you, but your support alone is more than enough. I’ll try handling this on my own.”

After all, this was my personal business venture. It wouldn’t feel right to lean on Mr. Juuzou too much.

At my reply, Mr. Juuzou sank into his sofa. A slightly bitter expression crossed his face.  

“I see. Then go ahead and give it a try. But be careful—he’s not easy to deal with. He’s talented, but, well, troublesome.”

Ugh. Did he really have to say that now? Suddenly, I was feeling a lot more nervous.

Maybe I should have Mr. Juuzou come along after all—no, no. I’d already made a confident declaration. It would be embarrassing to backtrack now.

I had to focus, steel myself, and do this on my own.

“Well, I’ll be on my way, then.”

“Alright. I wish you a fruitful negotiation.”

Returning his nod with a somewhat stiff smile, I left the room.

◇◇◇

Colin and I headed to Mr. Shouda’s hospital room after stepping into the VIP lobby. Though spacious, it didn’t take long to reach his room. It was located fairly close to Mr. Juuzou’s.

I pressed the intercom button outside the door.

“Thank you for seeing me the other day. My name is Koutarou Matsunaga. I heard from Mr. Jounai that you had something to discuss with me, so I’ve come.”

“Thank you for taking the time. Please come in,” 

Mr. Shouda’s calm voice came over the intercom, followed by the sound of the door unlocking. 

Taking a deep breath, I steadied myself before stepping into the room with Colin.

The interior was spacious, fitting for a VIP room. Though, it lacked the opulence of Mr. Juuzou’s. The simplicity of the design stood out starkly, with functional furniture arranged neatly. The room’s starkness gave it a cold, sterile feel.

Standing in the center of the room, Mr. Shouda greeted us. He seemed to be in good condition, showing no signs of needing a cane.

“Thank you for coming, Matsunaga-san. I had to ask Juuzou to connect us because there’s something I must ask you—oh, and who might this be?”

“I’m sorry. This is my sister’s daughter. I’m looking after her right now, and she’s at an age where I can’t leave her alone…”

“I’m Colin. Nice to meet you!” 

“Nice to meet you too, Colin-chan. I rarely have visitors, so it’s nice to have some liveliness around here. Now, would you like something to drink?”

“Oh, there’s no need to trouble yourself.”

“I’d like juice! Orange is my favorite!”

“Haha, I happen to have some orange juice. Make yourselves comfortable, and I’ll bring it right out.”

Feeling slightly awkward, I sat on the sofa. Though simple, the sofa felt luxurious. Its soft, smooth material was incredibly comfortable.

Mr. Shouda left the room briefly, returning soon after with a tray. He placed a freshly brewed cup of coffee in front of me and a glass of orange juice before Colin.

As I took a sip of the aromatic coffee—far superior to instant—Mr. Shouda spoke up, watching Colin drink her juice with a smile.

“The results of my regular check-up have come in.”

It seemed the conversation was about to take a serious turn. Mr. Shouda picked up a sheet of paper from the table and turned it toward me.

“…The cancer that had metastasized throughout my body disappeared, and even the primary tumor in my lungs shrank significantly.”

“Is that so? Congratulations!”

“Thank you… though I must say, you don’t seem surprised.”

“What do you mean?”

“I was a terminal cancer patient, wasn’t I? Such a sudden improvement shouldn’t be possible. My attending doctor was trying to hide his disbelief, but even he seemed too astonished to be entirely happy.”

“Is that so? I’ve heard stories of miraculous recoveries on TV. I don’t think it’s entirely impossible.”

Learning from my experience with Mr. Juuzou, I decided not to immediately attribute the recovery to the potion. Instead, I wanted to ease Mr. Shouda into realizing the truth without overwhelming him.

“TV is full of fiction. When my cancer was first diagnosed, I tried all sorts of things. But none of them worked. …….But then, it turned out the miracle was closer than I thought.”

“What do you mean?”

“Juuzou, of course. Until recently, he’d say things like, ‘I’ll go ahead and wait for you on the other side’. He was on the verge of death himself. But before I knew it, he was jogging in the mornings. Naturally, I asked him what had happened. But all he would say was that it must have been a miracle.”

Mr. Shouda shrugged, exasperated, but his narrowed eyes gleamed sharply. He then abruptly cut to the chase.

“—The water that Riori-chan made me drink the other day. I believe that’s what caused my cancer to shrink. Thinking back, the moment I drank it, the fatigue in my body vanished. And I could walk without a cane. …Am I right, Matsunaga-san?”

It seemed he had deduced the truth on his own. That made things simpler. I nodded.

“You’re correct. That water—a potion—has healing properties. I wasn’t certain how effective it would be, but I’m glad to see it worked even on cancer.”

“Hmm, so your sales pitch caught me after all. …And where exactly did you obtain this potion? Can you continue to procure it?”

“I’m afraid I can’t disclose the source. However, I can sell it to you.”

Since I planned to sell potions to others as well, I intended to keep the details as vague as possible. But—

“…Not knowing the source is problematic,” 

Mr. Shouda said, furrowing his brow and speaking earnestly.

“I had resigned myself to death once, but living longer has sparked new desires. Right now, I’m willing to cling to any lifeline. Even in retirement, I still have influence, and it would be troublesome if potions were ever used as leverage or a threat. That’s why I need to know where they come from—for safety’s sake.”

Though his tone remained soft, there was a quiet intensity behind his words. However, I couldn’t back down either.

“I’m sorry, but I cannot share the source.”

“I’ll promise to buy only from you, as long as there’s no trouble—no matter how high the price.”

“Even so, I must decline.”

“…….I see. Then it can’t be helped.”

Just as I breathed a sigh of relief, thinking he had accepted my response, Mr. Shouda clapped his hands.

Suddenly, the door behind us burst open. Several large men in black suits and sunglasses stormed in. They surrounded us in an instant. Mr. Shouda’s thin lips curved into a satisfied smile.

“So, will you reconsider my request now?”

+++

# 224. As a Professional——

Surrounded by men in black suits looking down at me, I assumed they were Mr. Shouda’s bodyguards or perhaps enforcers. Their stance alone exuded a presence that screamed of professional expertise in handling rough situations. 

I had dealt with my fair share of lowlife thugs who relied on intimidation and threats. Sadly, I was somewhat accustomed to them. But the silent pressure from these men in black was something else entirely. It caused cold sweat to bead on my forehead.

Mr. Shouda was keeping the men in black at bay. He spoke calmly. 

“If you wish to continue living peacefully without fear, I won’t do anything to harm your interests. So, I ask you again.” 

“…My answer remains the same.” 

For a moment, I wondered if I should just tell him everything if he promised not to spread it. But I, too, just want to live a peaceful life. And I can’t afford to show weakness to someone who leads with the threat of violence. 

I glanced around at the men in black once more. Their expressions didn’t shift; behind their sunglasses, their sharp gazes were locked onto me. They were focused on catching even the smallest of my movements. 

I didn’t want to imagine what might happen if I made any suspicious moves. Worst case, I’d end up as fish food by tomorrow. Feeling the tension, I unconsciously gulped. Which seemed to amuse Mr. Shouda, who spoke again. 

“I see. If your answer doesn’t change, then I have no choice but to move on to the next stage.” 

With a snap of his fingers, the men in black deftly slipped their hands into their jackets. Whatever they grabbed was hidden from view, but it wasn’t hard to guess what it was. No, I didn’t want to think about it. 

I hoped they wouldn’t resort to pulling triggers in a hospital room. But under these circumstances, anything seemed possible. Even the act of them preparing was a sufficient threat. And their intentions came across clearly. 

——But even so, I had resolved not to give in to threats. 

Negotiations had clearly fallen apart. From here, it was either a preemptive strike or a swift escape. Even if a sliver of magic were revealed, I could feign ignorance later. 

Alright, I’ve made up my mind. Suddenly, my head cooled, and I felt an odd sense of calm. 

Could this composure be due to my experience? 

——And then, I suddenly remembered. 

What about Colin? 

My mind had been so preoccupied with the men in black that I’d completely forgotten about Colin. It’s not an excuse, but she’d been quiet this whole time. 

I turned to look at Colin sitting beside me. And— 

There she was, sipping orange juice contentedly. A blissful smile was on her face. 

When our eyes met, she gave me a bright, innocent grin. 

Uh… what? 

——Ah, I see. So ***that’s*** what’s going on? 

Ah, I get it now. So that’s how it is… 

It turns out I’d been completely deceived by the appearance of the men in black. Thinking they were professionals in rough business? What an embarrassing mistake. Apparently, Colin was the only real professional in the room. 

Relaxing my previously tense body, I sank back into the sofa and locked eyes with Mr. Shouda. I even crossed my legs—yes, rude, but so what? It’s mutual. 

Of course, my provocative behavior made Mr. Shouda frown. 

“Oh dear, Mr. Matsunaga. Don’t get reckless now.” 

“I’m not being reckless. I’m just not going to talk. So, what will you do?” 

I smirked, trying to appear as fearless as possible. Mr. Shouda, however, grinned in amusement. 

“I see. So that’s your stance. Then there’s only one thing left to do.” 

Snapping his fingers again, the men in black simultaneously pulled out their items from inside their jackets— 

**_Bang! Bang! Bang! Bang!_** 

Deafening bursts erupted from all directions. 

The next moment, the sharp smell of gunpowder filled the air— 

“””“Happy birthday to you~! Happy birthday to you~! Happy birthday dear… MatsuNAGA-SAAAN! Happy birthday toOoOo yoOooOuuUuuu~!”””” 

The men in black burst into a full chorus of the birthday song. They were adding an annoyingly exaggerated vibrato to the final “to you~”. 

——Even though I was sure it was a bluff, I won’t deny that the sound of the party poppers startled my heart into jumping. For the record, Colin, who seemed to be seeing party poppers for the first time, watched them with sparkling eyes of curiosity. 

When the singing ended, Mr. Shouda beamed at me and spoke. 

“Happy birthday, Mr. Matsunaga. Did you enjoy the surprise? …Well then, gentlemen, you may leave now. Give my regards to the boss.” 

“””“Got it, sir!!”””” 

The men in black gave Mr. Shouda a sharp bow before briskly leaving the hospital room. 

“…It’s not my birthday today.”

“Haha, is that so? Seems I made a mistake.”

“Ah, a misunderstanding, was it? Then could you kindly explain the situation, including that part?” 

“Of course. But before that… I’m just glad Colin wasn’t scared. That was my only concern. Colin, were you okay? I’m sorry if it frightened you.” 

Actually, it was Colin’s calm demeanor that tipped me off to the bluff. Honestly, I shudder at the thought of what might’ve happened if Colin had decided to act before the men in black surrounded us. After all, they turned out to be amateurs. 

Colin, however, held up her now-empty glass and extended it toward Mr. Shouda. 

“That wasn’t scary at all! But if you feel bad about it, I’d like a refill of orange juice, please!” 

“Ha… haha… You’re quite the brave young lady. Alright, give me a moment.” 

With a wry smile, Mr. Shouda stood and walked toward another room. As I watched his back disappear, I leaned toward Colin and whispered softly. 

“You really saved me, Colin.” 

“I’m glad I could help!” 

She must have seen through everything from the start. Puffing out her chest proudly, Colin flashed me a brilliant smile. 

Guided by her reassuring expression, I finally relaxed. I let the tension drain from my shoulders and released a deep sigh of relief.

+++

# 225. Business Negotiation 2

“Okay, sorry to keep you waiting.” 

“Thanks for the juice!” 

Colin began happily sipping the orange juice placed on the table through a straw. Mr. Shouda narrowed his already thin eyes even further and watched for a moment. He then shifted his gaze to me. 

“……Now then, it was time for an explanation, right? First of all, let me say this: I haven’t lied about anything I’ve said so far. I really do need that potion. But I wanted to avoid a situation where I’d be blackmailed over it. That’s why I thought I’d get some dirt on you too. That was the surprise.” 

“By ‘surprise’, you mean that threat you pulled on me?” 

I said it bluntly without hesitation. I’m beyond formality at this point. But Mr. Shouda nodded without the slightest hint of remorse. 

“Yeah, exactly. I thought if you fell for it, we could be on equal footing…… but looks like I miscalculated.” 

“Uh, I see……” 

From my side, I never had any intention of using the potion as bait to do whatever I wanted in the first place. I’ve always considered the relationship between me, the seller, and Mr. Shouda, the buyer, to be equal. 

Mr. Shouda’s distrust of people is pretty intense. But if he’s someone who’s called Mr. Juuzou’s right-hand man, then maybe he’s had a lot of stuff happen to him in the past. It’s a world I don’t understand at all, though. 

“The men in black were actors from a theater troupe I know. I asked them to come under the pretense of setting up a little birthday surprise for a business partner. Of course, I didn’t tell them anything about you. They probably just think I’m some rich guy with bad taste.” 

“It’s definitely bad taste, that’s for sure. Did you not consider that I might get pissed off and stop selling the potion?” 

“Hmm, not really. Based on my past experiences, people who don’t fold under these kinds of threats usually have a big heart. They either laugh it off, punch me once and call it even, or use it cleverly to raise the terms—so, what’s your move?” 

Mr. Shouda stared into me like he was observing something. …Well, honestly, I was surprised. But I’m not mad at all. 

Of course, I’m not saying I have a big heart or anything. It’s just that I already had a safety margin in place from the start. So there’s no reason to get angry. 

Even so, it seems like Mr. Shouda has a bit of a history of pulling these kinds of stunts with other people too. Now I’m finally starting to understand what Mr. Juuzou’s warning meant… 

“Well then, Matsunaga-san. Let’s hear your answer.” 

Mr. Shouda asked, still looking directly at me. I couldn’t read at all what he was thinking behind those thin eyes—he was just quietly waiting for my reply. 

I’m not good at playing mind games, so I’ll just be straightforward. 

“Of course, I’ll sell it to you. But I’ll be adding a nuisance fee on top.” 

Naturally, I’ll sell the potion. I’ll also ride along with Mr. Shouda’s proposal and raise the price. Honestly, I hadn’t even thought of a nuisance fee until he mentioned it. But I could tell he was hoping to settle things around there too. 

Just as I expected, Mr. Shouda gave a faint smile at my proposal. 

“I see, agreed. So then… how much will the potion cost?” 

…Alright, now we’re getting to the main topic. 

Of course, I’ve already decided on the price of the potion. The price is exactly 3 million yen. That’s a price wealthy folks can afford. But this time, I’ll add the nuisance fee on top of that— 

“The same amount as the one you drank the other day, a paper cup’s worth… for five million yen.” 

“Fi-five million……??” 

For the first time, Mr. Shouda’s calm demeanor cracked. And his voice trembled in surprise. 

Ah, crap. Maybe that really was too expensive? I mean, it’s originally just tap water, so maybe I should’ve gone cheaper—no, no. If I back down here, I lose. Hang in there, me. 

Hiding my inner panic, I calmly answered again. 

“Yes. Five million yen.” 

“I see. Then, let’s hear the rest of the conditions.” 

“Huh? No, there aren’t any other conditions.” 

“……So basically, you’ve priced the potion at five million yen, is that it?” 

“Y-yeah. I believe it’s worth five million yen, though……?” 

Somehow, Mr. Shouda’s reaction wasn’t what I expected. He didn’t complain about the price being too high, but he didn’t seem convinced about it either. 

It felt like we were talking past each other. Just as I was about to ask what he meant, Mr. Shouda let out a slow breath. And with a softer expression than before, he began to speak. 

“I see. So you’re a much less greedy person than I had imagined…” 

“Um, what do you mean by that?” 

“I thought you were a dangerous man who wouldn’t hesitate to use any means to achieve his goals.” 

“Ehhh… What on earth made you think that about me…?” 

To my question, Mr. Shouda answered with a wry smile. 

“Haha, what made me think that… well, let’s see? At your age, you’ve already gotten close to Juuzou, one of the heavyweights in the Jounai Conglomerate, and even made a move on his granddaughter, Rio-chan. …And when I looked into it, I found out you’re also on good terms with Haruna-sama, the so-called ‘Witch of Jounai,’ and her precious foster daughter Seina, who never shows herself in public. A man with those kinds of connections is now approaching me. Naturally, I’d be suspicious about what your intentions were, right?” 

Huh? Wait, wait—what is this guy even saying? 

“I met Mr. Mr. Juuzou purely by chance, and my relationship with Aihara is nothing like what you’re imagining—she’s really just a junior to me. Also, Ms. Isezaki Haruna is my apartment landlady. And if we’re neighbors, it’s not strange that I’d be reasonably close with her foster daughter Seina, right?” 

“It’s a story that’s hard to believe. But it seems that’s how it is. Which means there was no need for me to resort to such forceful measures. …Haha, I had completely forgotten that such honest conversations even existed. Matsunaga-san, I’m a twisted old man. I’m deeply sorry for everything.” 

Up until now, Mr. Shouda hadn’t shown any signs of remorse. But for the first time, he bowed his head. 

“N-no, please raise your head. M-more importantly, about the five million yen—will that be alright?” 

“……In that case, I’ll speak frankly as well. Five million is ***too*** cheap—it honestly left me feeling a bit let down. I expected you to add more conditions.” 

Too cheap? We’re talking about five million yen for a single paper cup of water, you know? That’s around the average annual income in Japan! 

“You probably don’t know this, but the rent for this room per month is about that much.” 

“Eh!?” 

“The kind of people you’re going to be dealing with don’t even bat an eye at that kind of money. A mere five million? It doesn’t even need to be weighed against their health. …Well then, what do you say? Want to up the price now after all? I don’t mind.” 

“……No, I’m not planning to raise the price any further. If I go too high, it could lead to trouble. ……Like, uh, this time.” 

“Haha, yeah, that might be true. …Say, if you’d like, I could handle future sales for you.” 

“You mean you would connect me with people who want the potion and take a brokerage fee?” 

“Not quite. I don’t need any fee. I would simply introduce you to people who genuinely need the potion. Didn’t I tell you? What I fear most is that you’ll stop selling the potion. As long as you need me, you’ll keep selling it, right?” 

“I don’t intend to be stingy with the potion… but, uh, can I think about the brokerage part for now?” 

“Of course, no problem.” 

I should talk to Mr. Juuzou about this first. This guy seems like he has a lot going on behind the scenes. And honestly, he’s kinda scary. I probably need to learn how to handle him properly. 

“Well then, since we’ve wrapped up the discussion, let’s end the business talk here. Would you mind selling me the potion now?” 

As soon as he sensed the conversation was over, Mr. Shouda neatly brought it to a close. 

You often hear that old folks love to talk endlessly. But the elderly people I know—my landlady and Mr. Juuzou—tend to be refreshingly brief. I really appreciate that. 

——A little while later, Mr. Shouda brought out a bundle of cash from a room in the back and plopped it down on the table. It was five neatly stacked bundles with paper bands. 

“So much money! Matsunaga-ojichan, how much orange juice can you buy with this?” 

Colin looked curiously at the bundle of cash on the table and asked. 

By the way, “Matsunaga-ojichan” is how Colin calls me in front of others. At first, she tried to call me “Uncle” like Isezaki-san does. But for some reason, Isezaki-san rejected that. 

“You could buy a mountain of orange juice with it. Let’s stop by a café later and have some tea.” 

“Yay!” 

Watching Colin, who was already looking forward to her *third* glass of orange juice, I reached into my bag— 

“Then, this is the potion I’ll be selling you today.” 

Pretending to take it out from my bag, I used my **[Storage Space]** to pull out a plastic bottle. I then poured its contents generously into the glass Mr. Shouda had prepared. 

“Thank you. Mind if I drink it right away?” 

“Of course.” 

Mr. Shouda tilted the glass and gulped down the potion in one go. 

This time, without coughing, he drained it completely. Placing a hand on his chest, he stayed still for a moment. He then slightly brightened his expression. 

“Hmm… As I thought, I feel like my body’s condition has improved even more. I wonder if the cancer might shrink further, or even disappear?” 

“Who knows… If it worked once, I think it’ll probably get better. But I’m not exactly sure. Ah, just in case, please keep quiet about the potion, alright?” 

“Of course. Like Juuzou, I’ll just vaguely call it a miracle or something. Ahh… I’m actually looking forward to my next checkup now. I never thought the day would come when I’d look forward to something I used to dread.” 

Mr. Shouda shook his shoulders in amusement for a while. But he suddenly began rummaging through his jacket pocket. 

“…Sorry, I can’t hold back anymore. Just one—may I?” 

What Mr. Shouda took out from his chest pocket was an elegant cigar case and lighter. Apparently, he wanted a smoke. 

“Ah, please go ahead.” 

“I will endure!” 

Colin took a deep breath and then held it completely still. It seems tobacco exists even in the other world, and she’s not fond of it. Still, the fact that she had no intention of leaving the area must be part of her bodyguard duties. A true professional. 

Nodding at our responses, Mr. Shouda took a cigarette from the cigar case and lit it with practiced ease. 

He then took a deep inhale and slowly exhaled the smoke. As it drifted through the air, Mr. Shouda murmured, 

“I had thought I’d like to take one last drag with my lungs full before I died. But once your lungs are actually diseased, you can’t even smoke even if you want to. That’s what I regretted the most. Finally, I was able to have that long-awaited smoke. Thank you, Matsunaga-san. Ahh… It’s good…” 

There was a glint in Mr. Shouda’s thin eyes, and his voice trembled. 

I started selling potions just as a way to make money. But seeing people up close like this, truly happy—it’s not such a bad thing after all. 

——And so, I had finally succeeded in earning a huge income in Japan: five million yen.

+++

#  226. Return to the Capital City After a While

“Haa… I see. So that guy Shouda really did screw things up, huh…”

Mr. Juuzou sighed in exasperation. 

Right after I sold the potion, I came straight to report to Mr. Juuzou.

“Yeah, well, that’s right… So, Shouda-san offered to act as a mediator for potion customers. But what do you think about that, Juuzou-san?”

“Let’s see… Hmm, if Shouda was the one who brought it up, it’s probably best to leave it to him. He’s twisted, but he’s also a capable man. When someone’s useful, you use them.”

“Umm, well… I kind of feel bad saying this about someone you know, but… is it really okay to trust Shouda-san?”

Honestly, I’m nothing but anxious. But unlike me, Mr. Juuzou answered with a hearty laugh.

“Hahaha, I don’t blame you for thinking that, Matsunaga-kun. But Shouda isn’t the kind of man to betray someone he’s acknowledged. I guarantee it. Besides, now that he’s healthy again, he’s probably bored too. So go ahead and use him as much as you like.”

“R-Right…”

So this is what they mean by a man of great character, huh? 

I’m really impressed by how generous Mr. Juuzou is, but still… it doesn’t erase my anxiety.

I don’t even feel like I’ve been acknowledged. And besides, Mr. Shouda totally looks like a stereotypical narrow-eyed schemer. He’s just screaming betrayal flag. 

I know these things.

…That said, it’s exhausting to keep dealing with quirky old men going forward. 

Selling potions while triggering these kinds of events every time would probably give me stomach ulcers from stress. I just want to make money as easily as possible.

――And so, in the end, I made a U-turn back to Mr. Shouda’s hospital room and asked him to act as the mediator.

By the way, the hospital room was already full of cigarette smoke. 

Even if you’ve got potions, please take care of your health first.

◇◇◇

**The next day.** 

Instead of going for the usual materials transport job, I teleported to the other world for personal reasons. 

Colin and Isezaki-san had just come back from school. So they also came with me.

Our destination was the capital city—Dornesia Trading Company. 

It’s the famous merchant company specializing in monster materials. It was the one that helped me out when I sold the Earth Dragon before.

Lately, I’ve been running low on my stock of monster meat that supports my diet. 

They sell monster meat at Reymar Trading Company in Grandain too. But when it comes to variety, the specialist Dornesia Company has the better selection.

The landlady said she wants to eat something unusual too. So I figured we might as well come over here.

“――Matsunaga-sama and madam! It’s been a while! What kind of monster have you brought today????”

As soon as we were led into the reception room by the receptionist, the one who came right away was the plump middle-aged man—Mr. Carant, the head of Dornesia Trading Company.

(Note: Refer to C74 for the their first encounter with Carant.)

“A-Ah, no, we’re not here to sell today. We’re here to buy…”

“Fweh, is that so…!? Haaaaa…”

Mr. Carant slumped his shoulders and shrank his big body in disappointment. 

Looks like, since I brought an Earth Dragon before, both he and the receptionist got their hopes up.

But seeing him that sad made me feel kind of bad, so…

“I do have a little something I could sell…”

“Oh! What is it, what kind of meat!?”

I remembered something I had. And when I told him, Mr. Carant perked right up and leaned his face in close. 

He really does love monsters, huh.

“It’s a Treant. I managed to get a bit of it the other day.”

It was the corpse of the Treant that attacked us when I climbed the mountain with Maristel. 

Apparently, it sells for a good price. And Isezaki-san—who didn’t know that—got teased about it.

Seems like she remembered that, too. As she scrunched her eyebrows with a deep frown.

“Oho, a Treant! I’m very interested! May I see it right away? Come, come, right this way! Come, come, come!”

Urged on by Carant, we headed over to the unusually large marble table set up at the edge of the reception room.

Even though the reception room was lavishly decorated, this table had a rugged design and kind of stood out—but I guess this is what it’s used for.

Impressed, I started laying out the Treant corpse from my **[Storage Space]**. 

Of course, I couldn’t put everything on it. But it should be enough for just a look.

“Treants aren’t that strong. But they have a certain rarity. That’s because they can only live in lands rich in magic essence… Hmm, the way the branches are attached is very good… I see, I see—”

While giving commentary, Mr. Carant carefully inspected each of the Treant’s trunks. Which had been split in two or smashed to pieces.

“Hmm… The way it was taken down is truly excellent! It was defeated in a single blow. Matsunaga-sama, who was it that did this? Among the adventurers I know—‘Shuren of the Storm,’ ‘Bordeaux the Fierce Claw’… no, this powerful strike could even be the work of ‘Agras the Ogre Axe’…!?”

“N-No, no. I’m sorry, but I can’t reveal where I got it…”

Mr. Carant started naming adventurers with impressive titles. But of course, I couldn’t tell him that it was done by “Matsunaga the Unemployed”. I could only dodge with a wry smile.

“I see, that’s unfortunate… In that case, I’ll look at the rest of the Treant later—do you have anything else?”

Mr. Carant asked, his eyes sparkling. Hmm, well, I *do* have something, but…

“I’m sorry, but this is about all I’ve got…”

What I took out was the Scarlet Bird, completely turned into pitch-black charcoal by Isezaki-san’s **[Divine Thunder God Bolt]**. 

It was a high-tier monster, so I had brought it back just in case.

“This can’t be sold, right?”

“Hmm hmm… Is this a Scarlet Bird? As expected, with it burned to this extent, I can’t buy it, but—”

I knew it. I’ll probably just bury this somewhere later.

—or so I thought, but even so, Mr. Carant continued to observe the charred corpse with great interest.

“Hmm, hmm hmm… For the Scarlet Bird to be reduced to such a miserable state… The power of the attack was tremendous. To bring it down with such firepower—only one person comes to mind.”

Wow, this guy is really a hardcore adventurer geek. 

I casually listened. I was wondering what kind of name he’d come up with next.

Mr. Carant narrowed his eyes and muttered:

“This level of skill… it reminds me of the Great Saintess Seina.”

“”**PFFFT!!**“”

At Mr. Carant’s sudden words, Isezaki-san and I simultaneously burst out laughing and looked at each other.

+++

# 227. Memory Talk

“_Ahem!_ G-Great Saintess Seina… is it?” 

While I covered up my snort and asked, Mr. Carant deeply nodded. 

“Yes. When you think of the Great Saintess Seina, you think of healing holy magic. But, she could also use attack magic. I don’t think that part is very well known though.” 

“I-I see. Is that so…” 

Of course, I know that since I’ve seen it many times myself — but maybe because my response was a bit indifferent, Mr. Carant raised one eyebrow with a hum. 

“Oh? It seems you don’t believe me. But… actually, I, Karant, have seen with my own eyes the scene where Lady Seina subjugated a monster!” 

He puffed up his plump belly even more. He was looking somewhat proud. I glanced sideways at Isezaki-san. She was shaking her head furiously. But Mr. Carant didn’t notice and continued. 

“I still clearly remember that day… About ten years ago, I heard a rumor that a Wyvern had crash-landed for some reason and was retrieved in a nearby village. So I went there to purchase it. Hiring guards would reduce profits, and taking too long to prepare would let other merchants beat me to it — thinking that, foolishly, I set out with no guards. I head there with just an empty carriage and a subordinate acting as a coachman.” 

Wyverns are flying monsters. Apparently, they aren’t as strong as something-Dragon types. But because they fly, they’re hard to catch, and their materials are rather rare. 

Seems like young Mr. Carant was quite reckless. Hard to imagine that side of him from his current dignified appearance. 

“But on the way, we were attacked by a Wyvern that had gotten separated from its group. To be attacked by the very monster I was trying to purchase parts from — such irony. That one seemed to be the one that had fought with the mentioned Wyvern and was covered in wounds. It was very agitated. If we had guards, maybe we could’ve driven it away or defeated it. But with just two amateurs, there was nothing we could do. First the horse was killed, then my subordinate was injured. And finally, it was my turn — just at that moment, Lady Seina, who was returning to the domain capital after a healing tour, appeared.” 

Really? I glanced at Isezaki-san. Then, as if she remembered something, her eyes and mouth opened wide. 

“Lady Seina stood in front of me. She ignored the knight’s attempt to stop her, and she swung her arm down at the charging Wyvern. In the next moment, a flash of light shot from her and struck the Wyvern directly. And a loud roar echoed. It was truly divine wrath — the Wyvern was instantly charred black and slammed into the ground. That scene is something I will never forget…!” 

Mr. Carant passionately clenched his fist and spoke with excitement. Then— 

“I-Is that sooo! That’s amazing! Well then, Husband? Shall we proceed with the purchase now?” 

Isezaki-san spoke rapidly and tugged hard on my sleeve. 

What is it? Maybe she has something to do? But Mr. Carant, all wrapped up in his story, didn’t notice and kept talking. 

“After the Wyvern was defeated, I was so shocked that I fell on my butt and was glued to the spot. Then, Lady Seina walked up to me boldly and shouted, ‘Mister! Are you stupid going without guards? Do you want to die that badly!?’ From her outfit, I could tell right away she was the Great Saintess. But I was so overwhelmed by her words and intensity that I couldn’t say anything. I just stood there dumbfounded.” 

That image doesn’t quite match the calm Isezaki-san of now… I thought, and then the force pulling my sleeve weakened. Isezaki-san looked down, embarrassed. 

Seems like she didn’t want that part of the story heard. But it’s just a childhood story, no need to be that bothered. 

“Afterward, Lady Seina even healed my subordinate and, since we’d lost our horse, let us accompany her back to the domain capital. The knight guards were reluctant. But Lady Seina persuaded them, it seemed. On the way, when she heard I was in the monster trading business, Lady Seina became very curious and asked many questions. I still remember how innocent and childlike she was, and it was very heartwarming.” 

“I see, Lady Seina was a very kind person,” 

I said while looking at Isezaki-san. Her face still red, she kept her eyes down. 

“Yes. And from that event, I finally realized the importance of having guards. I also became very interested in the adventurers who work as guards. And I wanted to learn more about their jobs and experiences.”

I see, so the reason Mr. Carant is so knowledgeable about adventurers is because of that experience. 

Though I didn’t expect Isezaki-san to be involved. The world is surprisingly small.

“It is unfortunate that Lady Seina has passed away… Even so, the fact that there are still magic users like her out there, I find deeply moving.” 

Mr. Carant gazed sentimentally at the nicely roasted Scarlet Bird. 

But then he suddenly changed his expression and, looking a little shy, asked me with upturned eyes, 

“U-Um… would it be possible to tell me who the adventurer that defeated the Scarlet Bird was…?” 

“I’m sorry, but…” 

Even though that adventurer is right in front of him, of course I can’t say that. 

But since we’ve gone through similar conversations before, Mr. Carant gave up easily. 

“I see, that’s unfortunate but it can’t be helped. Even so… Lady Levia really is connected to many capable people. I truly envy her. …I’ve heard she is actively working toward restarting the magic stone mine.” 

“So it seems. Word has reached the domain capital as well, huh.” 

“Yes, of course. There was talk of our company opening a branch in the settlement that will be built near the mana stone mine. But we haven’t been granted permission, which is quite frustrating.” 

“Permission, you say? I don’t think Lady Levia would reject the idea of a merchant company opening a branch…” 

After all, it’s Lady Levia who’s been actively gathering people for the mine’s reopening. For the sake of development, merchants are also necessary. And there are already people who’ve started doing business. 

When I tilted my head, Mr. Carant replied with a troubled look, 

“Well, actually, it’s because of Lady Delixir’s will… There’s been an official order forbidding companies that start doing business in the magic stone mine from opening shops in the domain capital.” 

“Huh, I see…..…” 

It seems Levia’s older sister, Delixir, is involved. 

If that’s the case, then this kind of obstruction might not be the only one. 

Things are starting to smell fishy…

“So then, I wish Lady Levia great success. …Ah, sorry, the conversation ran long. Let’s move on to the business negotiations—”

And so, after wrapping up the talk, we proceeded with the business deal with Mr. Carant—as a result, the Treant was sold for 3 million G.

When you consider that the Earth Dragon I brought in on my first visit sold for 100 million G, it feels like a smaller amount. But that one was just an exception—this is still a very high price.

And just as originally planned, I also proceeded with purchasing monster meat. 

The landlady had said she wanted to try eating bat-type monsters. And just as she wished, there was meat from a bat-type monster called a Shadow Bat. So I went ahead and bought it. 

Apparently, even in this world, it’s considered a bizarre food. And Mr. Carant’s face stiffened slightly. But since I won’t be the one eating it, it’s fine. ……….Though, maybe I’ll be made to eat it too…?

With a bit of that worry in mind, I bought a large amount of monster meat. And we were seen off by Mr. Carant as we left the Dornesia Trading Company.

+++

# 228. A Casual Stroll Through the Domain Capital

Having finished our business with the Dornesia Company, we decided to enjoy the domain capital after a long while. So, first, we decided to visit the furniture store affiliated with the Dornesia Company.

Apparently, that furniture store was selling a table made from an Earth Dragon’s shell. And Mr. Carant had strongly recommended that we visit it.

I was also curious to see what had become of the materials I sold. So, upon visiting the furniture store, we found that the Earth Dragon-made table was proudly displayed in the most prominent exhibition space.

That table was large enough to seat six people. It had a solid, dignified presence.

The tabletop was carefully crafted from the deep-colored shell of the Earth Dragon we defeated at that time. And the way the hue subtly changed depending on the angle kept the viewer from growing bored. The Earth Dragon reliefs carved into the edge of the table were stylish, too.

It seemed like a very expensive piece—and sure enough, its price was a staggering ten million G.

Moreover, two of them had already been sold. And this one was apparently the last. Seems like money really does exist where it exists.

Of course, I was interested. But even so, ten million G for a table is too expensive. And it’s way too big to put in my room. I gave a polite smile to the clerk who approached rubbing his hands together and quickly left the furniture store.

After that, we strolled around the domain capital. However, we made sure to walk away from the central area.

That’s because before, we had a close call with Derixir at a high-class restaurant, which turned into a bit of a hassle. It would be wise not to get too close to areas where nobles come and go.

As I thought about that while walking, we gradually moved away from the glittering atmosphere of the center. A lively, cluttered downtown scene began to spread before us.

Street stalls selling suspicious trinkets that could be either junk or treasures. Food stalls drawing in customers with delicious smells and loud voices. And kids playing tag.

Even though it’s the domain capital, the outskirts aren’t any different from Grandain. As I was taking in that kind of scenery—

“Oh? Hey!”

Suddenly, a voice called out from behind. It was a deep male voice.

Come to think of it, while there may be no nobles in this area, that doesn’t mean the security is good either. I must’ve caught the attention of some shady guy—I stiffened my face and turned around—

“I knew it! Ain’t that you, Matsunaga-san!?”

There stood a burly man with a beard, smiling at me.

Of course, I knew who he was. He was the leader of the adventurer group Lady Levia had hired as escorts during our journey to the domain capital before.

I had thought “leader” referred to his role as the one in charge. But it turned out that “Leader” was his actual name, which made things a bit confusing.

(Note: See C48 for their first encounter with “Leader”.)

“Long time no see, Leader-san.”

“Yeah! Been a while! What’re you doing in a place like this?”

“Oh, we just came to the capital to buy a few things. And figured we’d take a little stroll while we were at it.”

“Ah, that’s right, you’re a traveling merchant, huh. You always carry so little that I nearly forgot. And the missus, long time no see to you too. Still a beauty as ever—that kid I haven’t seen before though, could it be your child?”

“C-Child!? That’s right! Actually, yes! This child is the crystallization of love between me and my husband—”

“This child is a bodyguard Lady Levia assigned to us. Things have been a bit dangerous lately, you see.”

“Muuuuh!”

Isezaki-san puffed out her cheeks in frustration as I cut in. Seems she’s still fully committed to the husband-and-wife setup. But if we add any more settings, it’s going to get too complicated. So let’s stop there.

“I’m Colin! Nice to meet you!”

“Yeah, likewise.”

Leader cheerfully replied to Colin’s bow. He was scratching his bearded chin.

“She seems kinda young to be a bodyguard, though… but hey, who knows what nobles are thinking, right? Well, whatever. Still, seems like you’re as close as ever with Lady Levia.”

“Yes, thanks to her, we’ve been given quite a few favors.”

“That so, huh. That’s a great help for a merchant. …By the way, since it’s been a while, how about we grab a bite together? My treat.”

Leader nodded toward a nearby skewer stand. I had some things I wanted to ask too, so it was perfect. We followed him to the food stand.

◇◇◇ 

After being treated to a mountain of skewered Earth Rat meat at the food stall, we moved to a nearby bench. The moment we sat down, Leader looked up at us with upturned eyes. 

“…Uhh, it’d be real nice if you could cover the drinks… *glance glance*” 

Yeah, other stalls were selling drinks, but he passed them by. So I figured he’d do this. 

I really don’t want to see a bearded middle-aged man begging cutely. I decided to just give in to his request quickly. 

“Sure. But we just ran out of cola, you see…” 

“Ehh!? You don’t have cola…?” 

Leader dropped his shoulders with a face like he was about to die. 

So he ***was*** after the cola. But there hasn’t been any reason to stockpile it lately. So I’d already finished drinking what I had. What I did have was— 

“Ah, right. Back when you were our escort, didn’t you complain about not being able to drink alcohol? I do have some booze, but… I guess drinking in the middle of the day is no good?” 

“Huh, booze? Then booze it is! I’m not working anymore today!” 

Leader leaned forward eagerly. He looked even happier than when he heard about cola. In that case, no problem. 

I pulled out a chilled canned beer from **[Storage Space]**. I then poured it into a paper cup before handing it over. Leader peeked into the cup. 

“Ooh… Is this ale?” 

“Well, something similar.” 

Technically, it’s different. But let’s not fuss over the details. 

“Guess I’ll try a sip—” 

Leader tilted the cup all at once. 

“—!!” 

His eyes widened. And he gulped down the entire contents of the paper cup in one go. Then— 

“*_BUUUUUUUUUUUUUURP!*_” 

He let out a massive belch. 

Startled by the sudden roar, Colin crouched into a wary stance. And Isezaki-san froze in place with a forced smile. Come to think of it, he let out a similar burp when he drank cola too… 

Meanwhile, completely unaware of those around him, Leader’s eyes lit up. 

“What the hell is this! Like cola-level strong carbonation, with a crisp bitterness and throat-feel different from ale! And it’s ice cold…! This is the best booze I’ve ever had!!” 

Right, drinks are normally served at room temperature here, huh. There _are_ beers on Earth that are served warm. But still, beer is best ice cold. 

“I’m glad you liked it. I’ve got more if you want seconds.” 

“I do, I do! Ahh… and the alcohol content is hitting pretty good too. This booze is amazing. Still, running into you by chance like this—guess I’m lucky today. This morning, Dag and Rochas went off to the brothel. So if they can’t have this, serves ‘em right. I’m gonna brag about this later, wahahaha!” 

Dag and Rochas are Leader’s party members. I’m happy he’s enjoying himself. But come on, don’t talk about that kind of stuff in front of Isezaki-san and Colin. Time to change the subject. 

“By the way, Leader-san. This is the first time we’ve been to the domain capital since we came with you all. Has anything changed around here since then?” 

“Oh, as a traveling merchant, you gotta stay sharp about the world’s movements. I’ll tell you what I know—” 

And with that, Leader began telling us about the recent state of the domain capital.

+++

# 229. Issue of the Capital City

Leader took a gulp of beer. And wiping his mouth with satisfaction, he began to speak. 

“Anyway… the hottest topic in the capital city right now is definitely the talk about the magic stone mine reopening. Rumor has it that it was Lady Levia who got it going again.” 

“Yes, that’s right. So the story’s spreading among adventurers too, huh?” 

“Of course. That mine’s been fought over ever since I was a kid. So when I heard that Lady Levia drove out the Digram guys and was reopening the mine, I seriously couldn’t believe my ears. I’ve hardly ever seen her in person. But she must be one amazing princess.” 

Leader spoke with admiration. He was stroking his chin thoughtfully. 

Then, Isezaki-san interrupted. 

“Um, Leader-san? It’s true that Lady Levia gave the order. But my husband also helped out with the magic stone mine. Actually, it’s no exaggeration to say he solved it all by himself. And he’s even more amazing! So please don’t get that part wrong!” 

With a sharp gesture, raising her index finger, Isezaki-san insisted strongly. 

No, I mean, I _do_ think I did my part. But saying I did it all by myself is kind of an exaggeration, right? 

Of course, Leader didn’t seem to believe Isezaki-san’s words. He gave a wry smile. 

“O-oh, is that so? So Matsunaga-san was involved too, huh.” 

“Yeah, well, just a little bit…” 

Hearing that, Isezaki-san looked at me with a face that clearly said, “Huh?” She was not satisfied at all. But I ignored it and kept the conversation going. Since I didn’t want it to get more complicated. 

“So, I’ve been hearing all sorts of good things because the mine’s reopening. But Leader-san, you’re not going to the magic stone mine? Is there some kind of decree not to go there?” 

“A decree? You mean from the nobles? Nothing like that’s been issued.” 

Apparently, unlike the merchant associations, there’s no pressure from Delixir. 

It’s true that adventurers, being drifters, are hard to control with power. 

For a moment, Leader looked sadly at his now-empty paper cup. He then spoke. 

“I heard a new town is being built at the foot of the magic stone mine. Actually, we found new party members too. So we were thinking of heading there soon. …But you know, all the skilled folks rushed ahead to the mine. That left the capital city’s adventurer guild flooded with leftover requests. And the guild staff begged us for help. So, we’ve been taking care of those requests. Well, it’s good money, so it’s not too bad.” 

Apparently, Leader’s party missed their chance to head to the mine because they lost members in the last escort mission. 

He didn’t seem too bothered by it, though. 

“Oh, right. Since you’re involved with the mine, Matsunaga-san, there’s something I want to give you a heads-up about.” 

“Huh? What is it?” 

“Among adventurers, there are scumbags who do nothing but shady stuff. Or trash who live easy lives by screwing over others. There’s talk that the merchant association in this town hired a bunch of those types and sent them to the magic stone mine. No telling what they’ll pull. So, if you’re planning to do business over there, you better be careful.” 

“…The capital’s merchant association sent people to the magic stone mine? Is that true?” 

“Yeah. One of those guys was bragging that he got hired by a big merchant association. So it’s probably legit. Something bugging you?” 

“From what I heard, there’s supposed to be a decree banning capital merchants from doing business at the magic stone mine…” 

“A decree? That’s weird. If I recall—” 

Leader suddenly leaned toward me and, looking around cautiously, whispered. 

“That merchant association… it’s called the Elgoa Association. It was Lady Levia’s older sister’s official merchant.” 

So that means only that merchant association gets special treatment. 

And what they’re doing is sending ill-behaved adventurers? 

That gives me nothing but a bad feeling. 

I should probably report this to Lady Levia or Holly, just in case. 

Even so… the fact that Leader lowered his voice and looked around suggests that Delixir has become an untouchable name even among adventurers. 

Well, considering the outrageous scene at that restaurant before, I guess that makes sense. 

“I see. I’ll keep that warning in mind. Leader-san, want a refill?”

“Oh, really? I can have more? I’ll drink, I’ll drink! Man, today’s the best day ever! Oh, Matsunaga-san, you guys should eat lots of grilled skewers too!” 

Like that, I treated Leader to plenty of beer as payment for the information. And while drawing out more stories, I left the capital city. 

◇◇◇ 

After teleporting from the capital city with **[Dimensional Teleport]**, we arrived at Lady Levia’s castle. We then shared with Holly, who welcomed us, the information we had gathered in the capital. 

According to Holly, it was indeed true that the Elgoa Merchant Association in question was on friendly terms with Delixir. They often used her influence to push business deals and negotiations through forceful methods. 

Because of that, they had a terrible reputation among those involved. Even so, it remained one of the top merchant associations in the capital. 

That shows just how much influence backing from a noble carries. 

Of course, in return, the Elgoa Association follows Delixir’s orders completely. And Holly believes that Delixir is most likely pulling the strings from behind in this matter as well. 

But then, you might think—why not just have Lady Levia revoke the Elgoa Association’s commercial rights in the magic stone mine and nip the trouble in the bud? 

However, it seems it’s not that simple. 

Let’s say a noble uses their authority to exclude a merchant association. If that action is seen as tyranny, other merchants may become wary, pull back, or slow down their involvement. That in turn could cause major delays in business progress. 

And they can’t afford to negatively impact the mine development, which they want to advance as soon as possible. 

Because of that, the conclusion was that—for now—they had no choice but to keep an eye on the Elgoa Association.

◇◇◇ 

After returning to Japan, we immediately handed over the souvenir, Shadow Bat meat, to the landlady. 

Of course, the landlady was overjoyed at the long-awaited bat meat. 

I tried to gently refuse. But the high-spirited landlady pushed through. And in the end, I ended up eating the Shadow Bat with them. 

The landlady and Colin bit into the whole deep-fried Shadow Bat from the head with gusto. They were munching happily and saying how delicious it was. 

Meanwhile, Isezaki-san and I barely managed to eat only the br3ast meat—the part that looked possibly edible—after having it made into karaage (fried chicken style). We somehow got it down. 

I’d finally gotten used to eating rats. But eating bats was still too much. 

What’s worse, there was a whole grilled bat sitting proudly on the plate in front of us. It was giving off the vibe that some dark ritual was about to begin. 

Even Isezaki-san, who was raised in another world, seemed to struggle with this one. 

With vacant eyes, she just moved her mouth mechanically. Her expression alone spoke volumes about how she felt. 

I’m sure I had the same look on my face too. 

By the way, the meat was crunchy. It was like chewing on cartilage…..

+++

# 229. The Banquet of Darkness (Short Story)

In the last chapter, the meal scene with the landlord was glossed over for pacing reasons. But since it’s a fun moment, I decided to include it here as a bonus short story. 

It’s a quick read, so please enjoy it ＼(^o^)／ 

— Foreword —

“Oh, Landlady. This is a souvenir.” 

After returning from the other world, we visited the Isezaki residence and handed over the package of Shadow Bat meat. 

However, upon seeing the package, the landlady briefly furrowed her brows as if troubled. 

“Hey, Matsunaga-kun. I appreciate the thought, but you don’t always have to go out of your way like this, okay? Seina, you should’ve told him that too.” 

“Um, Grandma… about that, this time, well…” 

Isezaki-san mumbled her words and gently peeled back a corner of the wrapping. 

At that moment, the bulging eyes and split mouth of the Shadow Bat were exposed. 

“Ma-Matsunaga-kun!? Don’t tell me this is…!” 

“Y-Yes. It’s the bat monster you wanted, the Shadow Bat.” 

“YEEEEEEEEEEAAAAAAHHH!! If that’s the case, say so sooner! Thanks, Matsunaga-kun! Tonight is a banquet sabbath!!” 

Suddenly yelling, the landlady snatched the package out of my hands. 

Alright, my job here is done!

“Well then, I’ll be heading—”
